<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Scientific opinion on climate change</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about scientific opinion regarding climate change, including a discussion of scientific <b>consensus</b> regarding its degree, causes and consequences. For public perception and controversy, see <a href="/wiki/Public_opinion_on_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Public opinion on climate change">Public opinion on climate change</a> and <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_controversy" title="Global warming controversy">Global warming controversy</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scientific_consensus_-_Earth%27s_climate_is_warming_(Temperature_Anomaly_%E2%84%83).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Scientific_consensus_-_Earth%27s_climate_is_warming_%28Temperature_Anomaly_%E2%84%83%29.png/450px-Scientific_consensus_-_Earth%27s_climate_is_warming_%28Temperature_Anomaly_%E2%84%83%29.png" width="450" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Scientific_consensus_-_Earth%27s_climate_is_warming_%28Temperature_Anomaly_%E2%84%83%29.png/675px-Scientific_consensus_-_Earth%27s_climate_is_warming_%28Temperature_Anomaly_%E2%84%83%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7f/Scientific_consensus_-_Earth%27s_climate_is_warming_%28Temperature_Anomaly_%E2%84%83%29.png 2x" data-file-width="735" data-file-height="529" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scientific_consensus_-_Earth%27s_climate_is_warming_(Temperature_Anomaly_%E2%84%83).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><small>From NASA’s Global Climate Change website - <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://climate.nasa.gov/">https://climate.nasa.gov/</a></small></div></div></div>
<p><b>Scientific opinion on climate change</b> is a judgment of scientists regarding the degree to which <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> is occurring, its likely causes, and its probable consequences. 
</p><p>A related&#8212;but not identical&#8212;term, "scientific <b>consensus</b> on climate change," is the <i>prevailing</i> view on climate change within the scientific community. The consensus is that:
</p>
<ul><li>Earth's climate has warmed significantly since the late 1800s,</li>
<li>Human activities (primarily <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions) are the <a href="/wiki/Attribution_of_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Attribution of climate change">primary cause</a>,</li>
<li>Continuing emissions will increase the likelihood and severity of <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming" title="Effects of global warming">global effects</a>, and that</li>
<li>We could manage future climate change impacts through intense efforts at <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">reducing further warming</a> while <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_adaptation" title="Climate change adaptation">preparing for any unavoidable</a> climate changes.</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_consensus">Scientific consensus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Scientific consensus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Several studies of the consensus have been undertaken.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Among the most-cited is a 2013 study of nearly 12,000 abstracts of peer-reviewed papers on climate science published since 1990, of which just over 4,000 papers expressed an opinion on the cause of recent global warming. Of these, 97% agree, explicitly or implicitly, that global warming is happening and is human-caused.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It is "extremely likely"<sup id="cite_ref-USGCRP4volI_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGCRP4volI-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> that this warming arises from "... human activities, especially emissions of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> ..."<sup id="cite_ref-USGCRP4volI_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGCRP4volI-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Earth" title="Atmosphere of Earth">atmosphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Natural change alone would have had a slight cooling effect rather than a warming effect.<sup id="cite_ref-AR4-warming-unequivocal_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AR4-warming-unequivocal-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ipcc1_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AmericasClimateChoices-2010-SciPanel_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmericasClimateChoices-2010-SciPanel-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This scientific opinion is expressed in <a href="/wiki/Systematic_review" title="Systematic review">synthesis reports</a>, by scientific bodies of national or international standing, and by <a href="/wiki/Surveys_of_scientists%27_views_on_climate_change" title="Surveys of scientists&#39; views on climate change">surveys of opinion among climate scientists</a>. Individual scientists, universities, and laboratories contribute to the overall scientific opinion via their <a href="/wiki/Peer_review" title="Peer review">peer-reviewed</a> <a href="/wiki/Scientific_journal" title="Scientific journal">publications</a>, and the areas of collective agreement and relative certainty are summarised in these respected reports and surveys.<sup id="cite_ref-Oreskes_consensus_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oreskes_consensus-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
The <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">IPCC</a>'s Fifth Assessment Report (AR5) was completed in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR5_Synth_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR5_Synth-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Its conclusions are summarized below:
</p>
<ul><li>"Warming of the climate system is unequivocal, and since the 1950s, many of the observed changes are unprecedented over decades to millennia".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>"Atmospheric concentrations of carbon dioxide, methane, and nitrous oxide have increased to levels unprecedented in at least the last 800,000 years".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Human influence on the climate system is clear.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR5_attribution_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR5_attribution-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It is extremely likely (95-100% probability)<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> that human influence was the dominant cause of global warming between 1951-2010.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR5_attribution_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR5_attribution-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>"Increasing magnitudes of [global] warming increase the likelihood of severe, pervasive, and irreversible impacts"<sup id="cite_ref-Summary_for_Policymakers_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Summary_for_Policymakers-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>"A first step towards adaptation to future climate change is reducing vulnerability and exposure to present climate variability"<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>"The overall risks of climate change impacts can be reduced by limiting the rate and magnitude of climate change"<sup id="cite_ref-Summary_for_Policymakers_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Summary_for_Policymakers-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Without new <a href="/wiki/Individual_and_political_action_on_climate_change" title="Individual and political action on climate change">policies to mitigate climate change</a>, projections suggest an increase in global mean temperature in 2100 of <a href="/wiki/4_Degrees_and_Beyond_International_Climate_Conference" title="4 Degrees and Beyond International Climate Conference">3.7 to 4.8&#160;°C</a>, relative to pre-industrial levels (<a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> values; the range is 2.5 to 7.8&#160;°C including climate uncertainty).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The current trajectory of global greenhouse gas emissions is not consistent with limiting global warming to below 1.5 or 2&#160;°C, relative to pre-industrial levels.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Pledges made as part of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2010 United Nations Climate Change Conference">Cancún Agreements</a> are broadly consistent with cost-effective scenarios that give a "likely" chance (66-100% probability) of limiting global warming (in 2100) to below 3&#160;°C, relative to pre-industrial levels.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Columbia_Glacier_in_Alaska.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Columbia Glacier in Alaska - 1986 vs 2011" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Columbia_Glacier_in_Alaska.jpg/220px-Columbia_Glacier_in_Alaska.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Columbia_Glacier_in_Alaska.jpg/330px-Columbia_Glacier_in_Alaska.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Columbia_Glacier_in_Alaska.jpg/440px-Columbia_Glacier_in_Alaska.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Columbia_Glacier_in_Alaska.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Columbia Glacier in Alaska, one of many vanishing around the world. Glacier retreat is one of the most direct and understandable effects of climate change.</div></div></div>
<p>National and international <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy of Sciences">science academies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Learned_society" title="Learned society">scientific societies</a> have assessed current <a href="/wiki/Scientific_opinion" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific opinion">scientific opinion</a> on <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>. These assessments are generally consistent with the conclusions of the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a>.
</p><p>Some scientific bodies have recommended specific policies to governments, and science can play a role in informing an effective response to climate change. Policy decisions, however, may require <a href="/wiki/Value_judgement" class="mw-redirect" title="Value judgement">value judgements</a> and so are not included in the scientific opinion.<sup id="cite_ref-tar_value_judgements_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_value_judgements-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NRC_on_policy_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC_on_policy-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>No scientific body of national or international standing maintains a formal opinion dissenting from any of these main points. The last national or international scientific body to drop dissent was the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Petroleum_Geologists" title="American Association of Petroleum Geologists">American Association of Petroleum Geologists</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AQAonAAPG_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AQAonAAPG-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> which in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-aapg19_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aapg19-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> updated its statement to its current non-committal position.<sup id="cite_ref-Oreskes07p68_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oreskes07p68-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Some other organizations, primarily those focusing on geology, also hold <a href="#Non-committal">non-committal positions</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Synthesis_reports">Synthesis reports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Synthesis reports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Synthesis reports are assessments of scientific literature that compile the results of a range of stand-alone studies in order to achieve a broad level of understanding, or to describe the state of knowledge of a given subject.<sup id="cite_ref-Integration_and_Synthesis:_Assessing_Climate_Change_Impacts_in_Northern_Canada_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Integration_and_Synthesis:_Assessing_Climate_Change_Impacts_in_Northern_Canada-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change_.28IPCC.29_2014"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change_(IPCC)_2014">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) 2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fifth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fifth Assessment Report">IPCC Fifth Assessment Report</a></div>
<p>The IPCC Fifth Assessment Report followed the same general format as the Fourth Assessment Report, with three Working Group reports and a Synthesis report.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR5_Synth_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR5_Synth-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Working Group I report (WG1) was published in September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR5_Synth_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR5_Synth-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The report's <i>Summary for Policymakers</i> stated that warming of the climate system is 'unequivocal' with changes unprecedented over decades to millennia, including warming of the atmosphere and oceans, <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">loss of snow and ice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a>. <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">Greenhouse gas</a> emissions, driven largely by economic and population growth, have led to greenhouse gas concentrations that are unprecedented in at least the last 800,000 years. These, together with other anthropogenic drivers, are "extremely likely" to have been the dominant cause of the observed global warming since the mid-20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC-AR5-SYN_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC-AR5-SYN-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It said that
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Continued emission of greenhouse gases will cause further warming and long-lasting changes in all components of the climate system, increasing the likelihood of severe, pervasive and irreversible impacts for people and ecosystems. Limiting climate change would require substantial and sustained reductions in greenhouse gas emissions which, together with adaptation, can limit climate change risks.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC-AR5-SYN_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC-AR5-SYN-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Reporting on the publication of the report, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> said that
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In the end it all boils down to risk management. The stronger our efforts to reduce greenhouse gas emissions, the lower the risk of extreme climate impacts. The higher our emissions, the larger climate changes we'll face, which also means more expensive adaptation, more species extinctions, more food and water insecurities, more income losses, more conflicts, and so forth.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In Washington, President Obama's science adviser, <a href="/wiki/John_Holdren" title="John Holdren">John P. Holdren</a>, cited increased scientific confidence "that the kinds of harm already being experienced from climate change will continue to worsen unless and until comprehensive and vigorous action to reduce emissions is undertaken worldwide."<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-AR5_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-AR5-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>It went on to say that <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> secretary general, had declared his intention to call a meeting of heads of state in 2014 to develop such a treaty. The last such meeting, in <a href="/wiki/2009_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2009 United Nations Climate Change Conference">Copenhagen in 2009</a>, the NY Times reported, had ended in disarray.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-AR5_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-AR5-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change_.28IPCC.29_2007"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change_(IPCC)_2007">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) 2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2007, the IPCC released a summary of the forthcoming <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fourth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fourth Assessment Report">Fourth Assessment Report</a>. According to this summary, the Fourth Assessment Report found that human actions are "very likely" the cause of global warming, meaning a 90% or greater probability. Global warming in this case was indicated by an increase of 0.75 degrees in average global temperatures over the last 100 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Warming_&#39;very_likely&#39;_human-made_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warming_&#39;very_likely&#39;_human-made-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fourth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fourth Assessment Report">IPCC Fourth Assessment Report</a> stated that:
</p>
<ul><li>Warming of the climate system is unequivocal, as evidenced by increases in global average air and ocean <a href="/wiki/Instrumental_temperature_record" title="Instrumental temperature record">temperatures</a>, the widespread melting of <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice" title="Ice">ice</a>, and rising global average <a href="/wiki/Current_sea_level_rise" class="mw-redirect" title="Current sea level rise">sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Most of the global warming since the mid-20th century is very likely due to <a href="/wiki/Attribution_of_recent_climate_change" title="Attribution of recent climate change">human activities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;VP9 (360P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;VP9 360P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;360p.vp9.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;640&quot; Higher than normal temperatures are shown in red and lower than normal temperatures are shown in blue.</div></div></div></li>
<li>Benefits and costs of climate change for [human] society will vary widely by location and scale.<sup id="cite_ref-parry_social_impacts_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parry_social_impacts-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Some of the effects in <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polar_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Polar region">polar regions</a> will be positive and others elsewhere will be negative.<sup id="cite_ref-parry_social_impacts_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parry_social_impacts-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Overall, net effects are more likely to be strongly negative with larger or more rapid warming.<sup id="cite_ref-parry_social_impacts_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parry_social_impacts-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The range of published evidence indicates that the net damage <a href="/wiki/Economic_impacts_of_climate_change" title="Economic impacts of climate change">costs of climate change</a> are likely to be significant and to increase over time.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Resilience_(ecology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Resilience (ecology)">resilience</a> of many <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_ecosystems" title="Climate change and ecosystems">ecosystems</a> is likely to be exceeded this century by an unprecedented combination of climate change, associated disturbances (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">flooding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">drought</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">wildfire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insects</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a>) and other <a href="/wiki/Global_change" title="Global change">global change</a> drivers (e.g. land-use change, <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>, fragmentation of natural systems, <a href="/wiki/Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation">over-exploitation</a> of resources).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p><i>The New York Times</i> reported that "the leading international network of climate scientists has concluded for the first time that global warming is 'unequivocal' and that human activity is the main driver, 'very likely' causing most of the rise in temperatures since 1950".<sup id="cite_ref-rosenthal_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rosenthal-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A retired journalist for <i>The New York Times</i>, William K. Stevens wrote: "The Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change said the likelihood was 90 percent to 99 percent that emissions of heat-trapping greenhouse gases like carbon dioxide, spewed from tailpipes and smokestacks, were the dominant cause of the observed warming of the last 50 years. In the panel's parlance, this level of certainty is labeled 'very likely'. Only rarely does scientific odds-making provide a more definite answer than that, at least in this branch of science, and it describes the endpoint, so far, of a progression.".<sup id="cite_ref-On_the_Climate_Change_Beat,_Doubt_Gives_Way_to_Certainty_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-On_the_Climate_Change_Beat,_Doubt_Gives_Way_to_Certainty-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> summarized the position on sea level rise:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>On sea levels, the report projects rises of 7 to 23 inches by the end of the century. An additional 3.9 to 7.8 inches are possible if recent, surprising melting of polar ice sheets continues.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Global_Change_Research_Program">U.S. Global Change Research Program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: U.S. Global Change Research Program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><i>Formerly: <a href="/wiki/Climate_Change_Science_Program" title="Climate Change Science Program">Climate Change Science Program</a></i></dd></dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Global_Change_Research_Program" title="U.S. Global Change Research Program">U.S. Global Change Research Program</a> reported in June 2009<sup id="cite_ref-globalchange_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalchange-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> that:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Observations show that warming of the climate is unequivocal. The global warming observed over the past 50 years is due primarily to human-induced emissions of heat-trapping gases. These emissions come mainly from the burning of fossil fuels (coal, oil, and gas), with important contributions from the clearing of forests, agricultural practices, and other activities.
</p></blockquote>
<p>The report, which is about the effects that climate change is having in the United States, also says:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Climate-related changes have already been observed globally and in the United States. These include increases in air and water temperatures, reduced frost days, increased frequency and intensity of heavy downpours, a rise in sea level, and reduced snow cover, glaciers, permafrost, and sea ice. A longer ice-free period on lakes and rivers, lengthening of the growing season, and increased <a href="/wiki/Water_vapor" title="Water vapor">water vapor</a> in the atmosphere have also been observed. Over the past 30 years, temperatures have risen faster in winter than in any other season, with average winter temperatures in the Midwest and northern Great Plains increasing more than 7&#160;°F (3.9&#160;°C). Some of the changes have been faster than previous assessments had suggested.
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arctic_Climate_Impact_Assessment">Arctic Climate Impact Assessment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Arctic Climate Impact Assessment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, the intergovernmental <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Council" title="Arctic Council">Arctic Council</a> and the non-governmental <a href="/wiki/International_Arctic_Science_Committee" title="International Arctic Science Committee">International Arctic Science Committee</a> released the synthesis report of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Climate_Impact_Assessment" title="Arctic Climate Impact Assessment">Arctic Climate Impact Assessment</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-Impacts_of_a_Warming_Arctic:_Arctic_Climate_Impact_Assessment_New_Scientific_Consensus:_Arctic_Is_Warming_Rapidly_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Impacts_of_a_Warming_Arctic:_Arctic_Climate_Impact_Assessment_New_Scientific_Consensus:_Arctic_Is_Warming_Rapidly-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Climate conditions in the past provide evidence that rising atmospheric carbon dioxide levels are associated with rising global temperatures. Human activities, primarily the burning of fossil fuels (coal, oil, and natural gas), and secondarily the clearing of land, have increased the concentration of carbon dioxide, methane, and other heat-trapping ("greenhouse") gases in the atmosphere...There is international scientific consensus that most of the warming observed over the last 50 years is attributable to human activities.<sup id="cite_ref-amap_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amap-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy">Policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Avoiding_dangerous_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Avoiding dangerous climate change">Avoiding dangerous climate change</a></div><p>
There is an extensive discussion in the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_literature" title="Scientific literature">scientific literature</a> on what policies might be effective in responding to climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_policy_assessment_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_policy_assessment-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Some scientific bodies have recommended specific policies to governments (refer to the later sections of the article).<sup id="cite_ref-nationalacademies6_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalacademies6-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">natural</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social sciences</a> can play a role in informing an effective response to climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-tar_value_judgements_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_value_judgements-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> However, policy decisions may require <a href="/wiki/Value_judgement" class="mw-redirect" title="Value judgement">value judgements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tar_value_judgements_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_value_judgements-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> For example, the <a href="/wiki/US_National_Research_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="US National Research Council">US National Research Council</a> has commented:<sup id="cite_ref-NRC_on_policy_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC_on_policy-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></p><blockquote><p>The question of whether there exists a "safe" level of concentration of greenhouse gases cannot be answered directly because it would require a value judgment of what constitutes an acceptable risk to human welfare and ecosystems in various parts of the world, as well as a more quantitative assessment of the risks and costs associated with the various impacts of global warming. In general, however, risk increases with increases in both the rate and the magnitude of climate change.</p></blockquote>
<p>This article mostly focuses on the views of natural scientists. However, social scientists,<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_policy_assessment_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_policy_assessment-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Medic" title="Medic">medical</a> experts,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> engineers<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_policy_assessment_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_policy_assessment-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and philosophers<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> have also commented on climate change science and policies. Climate change policy is discussed in several articles: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">climate change mitigation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_adaptation" title="Climate change adaptation">climate change adaptation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_engineering" title="Climate engineering">climate engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_global_warming" title="Politics of global warming">politics of global warming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_ethics" title="Climate ethics">climate ethics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_global_warming" title="Economics of global warming">economics of global warming</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statements_by_scientific_organizations_of_national_or_international_standing">Statements by scientific organizations of national or international standing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Statements by scientific organizations of national or international standing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_controversy#Mainstream_scientific_position,_and_challenges_to_it" title="Global warming controversy">Global warming controversy §&#160;Mainstream scientific position, and challenges to it</a></div>
<p>This is a list of scientific bodies of national or international standing, that have issued formal statements of opinion, classifies those organizations according to whether they concur with the IPCC view, are non-committal, or dissent from it. The California Governor's Office website lists nearly 200 worldwide scientific organizations hold the position that climate change has been caused by human action.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Concurring">Concurring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Concurring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Academies_of_science_.28general_science.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Academies_of_science_(general_science)">Academies of science (general science)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Academies of science (general science)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since 2001, 34 <a href="/wiki/National_academies" class="mw-redirect" title="National academies">national science academies</a>, three regional academies, and both the international <a href="/wiki/InterAcademy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="InterAcademy Council">InterAcademy Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Council_of_Academies_of_Engineering_and_Technological_Sciences" title="International Council of Academies of Engineering and Technological Sciences">International Council of Academies of Engineering and Technological Sciences</a> have made formal declarations confirming human induced global warming and urging nations to reduce emissions of greenhouse gases. The 34 national science academy statements include 33 who have signed joint science academy statements and one individual declaration by the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Polish Academy of Sciences">Polish Academy of Sciences</a> in 2007.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Joint_national_science_academy_statements">Joint national science academy statements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Joint national science academy statements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li>2001 Following the publication of the <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Third_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Third Assessment Report">IPCC Third Assessment Report</a>, seventeen national science academies issued a joint statement, entitled "The Science of Climate Change", explicitly acknowledging the IPCC position as representing the scientific consensus on climate change science. The statement, printed in an editorial in the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a></i> on May 18, 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-Editorial:_The_Science_of_Climate_Change_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Editorial:_The_Science_of_Climate_Change-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> was signed by the science academies of Australia, Belgium, Brazil, Canada, the Caribbean, China, France, Germany, India, Indonesia, Ireland, Italy, Malaysia, New Zealand, Sweden, Turkey, and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Science_of_Climate_Change_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Science_of_Climate_Change-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2005 The national science academies of the <a href="/wiki/G8" class="mw-redirect" title="G8">G8</a> nations, plus Brazil, China and India, three of the largest emitters of greenhouse gases in the developing world, signed a statement on the global response to climate change. The statement stresses that the scientific understanding of climate change is now sufficiently clear to justify nations taking prompt action, and explicitly endorsed the IPCC consensus. The eleven signatories were the science academies of Brazil, Canada, China, France, Germany, India, Italy, Japan, Russia, the United Kingdom, and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalacademies_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalacademies-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2007 In preparation for the <a href="/wiki/33rd_G8_summit" title="33rd G8 summit">33rd G8 summit</a>, the national science academies of the <a href="/wiki/G8%2B5" title="G8+5">G8+5</a> nations issued a declaration referencing the position of the 2005 joint science academies' statement, and acknowledging the confirmation of their previous conclusion by recent research. Following the <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fourth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fourth Assessment Report">IPCC Fourth Assessment Report</a>, the declaration states, "It is unequivocal that the climate is changing, and it is very likely that this is predominantly caused by the increasing human interference with the atmosphere. These changes will transform the environmental conditions on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> unless counter-measures are taken." The thirteen signatories were the national science academies of Brazil, Canada, China, France, Germany, Italy, India, Japan, Mexico, Russia, South Africa, the United Kingdom, and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-pik-potsdam_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pik-potsdam-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2007 In preparation for the <a href="/wiki/33rd_G8_summit" title="33rd G8 summit">33rd G8 summit</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Network_of_African_Science_Academies" title="Network of African Science Academies">Network of African Science Academies</a> submitted a joint "statement on sustainability, energy efficiency, and climate change"&#160;: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>A consensus, based on current evidence, now exists within the global scientific community that human activities are the main source of climate change and that the burning of fossil fuels is largely responsible for driving this change. The IPCC should be congratulated for the contribution it has made to public understanding of the nexus that exists between energy, climate and sustainability. </p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>The thirteen signatories were the science academies of <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/African_Academy_of_Sciences" title="African Academy of Sciences">African Academy of Sciences</a>, <sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li>2008 In preparation for the <a href="/wiki/34th_G8_summit" title="34th G8 summit">34th G8 summit</a>, the national science academies of the G8+5 nations issued a declaration reiterating the position of the 2005 joint science academies’ statement, and reaffirming "that climate change is happening and that anthropogenic warming is influencing many physical and biological systems." Among other actions, the declaration urges all nations to "(t)ake appropriate economic and policy measures to accelerate transition to a <a href="/wiki/Low_carbon_society" class="mw-redirect" title="Low carbon society">low carbon society</a> and to encourage and effect changes in individual and national behaviour." The thirteen signatories were the same national science academies that issued the 2007 joint statement.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalacademies5_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalacademies5-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2009 In advance of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Climate Change Conference 2009">UNFCCC</a> negotiations to be held in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> in December 2009, the national science academies of the G8+5 nations issued a joint statement declaring, "Climate change and sustainable energy supply are crucial challenges for the future of humanity. It is essential that world leaders agree on the emission reductions needed to combat negative consequences of anthropogenic climate change". The statement references the IPCC's Fourth Assessment of 2007, and asserts that "climate change is happening even faster than previously estimated; global CO<sub>2</sub> emissions since 2000 have been higher than even the highest predictions, Arctic sea ice has been melting at rates much faster than predicted, and the rise in the sea level has become more rapid." The thirteen signatories were the same national science academies that issued the 2007 and 2008 joint statements.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalacademies6_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalacademies6-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Polish_Academy_of_Sciences">Polish Academy of Sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Polish Academy of Sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In December 2007, the General Assembly of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Polish Academy of Sciences">Polish Academy of Sciences</a> (Polska Akademia Nauk), which has not been a signatory to <a href="#Joint_National_Science_Academy_Statements">joint national science academy statements</a> issued a declaration endorsing the IPCC conclusions, and stating:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>it is the duty of Polish science and the national government to, in a thoughtful, organized and active manner, become involved in realisation of these ideas.
</p><p>Problems of global warming, climate change, and their various negative impacts on human life and on the functioning of entire societies are one of the most dramatic challenges of modern times.
</p><p>PAS General Assembly calls on the national scientific communities and the national government to actively support Polish participation in this important endeavor.<sup id="cite_ref-Stanowisko_Zgromadzenia_Ogólnego_PAN_z_dnia_13_grudnia_2007_r_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stanowisko_Zgromadzenia_Ogólnego_PAN_z_dnia_13_grudnia_2007_r-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Additional_national_science_academy_and_society_statements">Additional national science academy and society statements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Additional national science academy and society statements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">American Association for the Advancement of Science</a> as the world's largest general scientific society, adopted an official statement on climate change in 2006: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The scientific evidence is clear: global climate change caused by human activities is occurring now, and it is a growing threat to society....The pace of change and the evidence of harm have increased markedly over the last five years. The time to control greenhouse gas emissions is now.<sup id="cite_ref-aaas_board_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaas_board-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australian_Scientific_and_Technological_Societies" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation of Australian Scientific and Technological Societies">Federation of Australian Scientific and Technological Societies</a> in 2008 published <i>FASTS Statement on Climate Change</i><sup id="cite_ref-FASTS_Statement_on_Climate_Change_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FASTS_Statement_on_Climate_Change-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> which states: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Global climate change is real and measurable...To reduce the global net economic, environmental and social losses in the face of these impacts, the policy objective must remain squarely focused on returning greenhouse gas concentrations to near pre-industrial levels through the reduction of emissions. The spatial and temporal fingerprint of warming can be traced to increasing greenhouse gas concentrations in the atmosphere, which are a direct result of burning fossil fuels, broad-scale deforestation and other human activity.</p></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Research Council">United States National Research Council</a> through its Committee on the Science of Climate Change in 2001, published <i>Climate Change Science: An Analysis of Some Key Questions</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-CCSAASKQ_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCSAASKQ-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> This report explicitly endorses the IPCC view of attribution of recent climate change as representing the view of the scientific community: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The changes observed over the last several decades are likely mostly due to human activities, but we cannot rule out that some significant part of these changes is also a reflection of natural variability. Human-induced warming and associated sea level rises are expected to continue through the 21st century... The IPCC's conclusion that most of the observed warming of the last 50 years is likely to have been due to the increase in greenhouse gas concentrations accurately reflects the current thinking of the scientific community on this issue.<sup id="cite_ref-CCSAASKQ_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCSAASKQ-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Society of New Zealand">Royal Society of New Zealand</a> having signed onto the first joint science academy statement in 2001, released a separate statement in 2008 in order to clear up "the controversy over climate change and its causes, and possible confusion among the public": <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The globe is warming because of increasing greenhouse gas emissions. Measurements show that greenhouse gas concentrations in the atmosphere are well above levels seen for many thousands of years. Further global climate changes are predicted, with impacts expected to become more costly as time progresses. Reducing future impacts of climate change will require substantial reductions of greenhouse gas emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_statement_from_the_Royal_Society_of_New_Zealand_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_statement_from_the_Royal_Society_of_New_Zealand-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a> of the United Kingdom has not changed its concurring stance reflected in its participation in <a href="#Joint_national_science_academies&#39;_statements">joint national science academies' statements</a> on anthropogenic global warming. According to the <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">Telegraph</a>, "The most prestigious group of scientists in the country was forced to act after fellows complained that doubts over man made global warming were not being communicated to the public".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In May 2010, it announced that it "is presently drafting a new public facing document on climate change, to provide an updated status report on the science in an easily accessible form, also addressing the levels of certainty of key components."<sup id="cite_ref-RS-CC_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-CC-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The society says that it is three years since the last such document was published and that, after an extensive process of debate and review,<sup id="cite_ref-Society_to_review_climate_message_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Society_to_review_climate_message-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Some_excitable_climate-change_deniers_just_don&#39;t_understand_what_science_is_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Some_excitable_climate-change_deniers_just_don&#39;t_understand_what_science_is-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> the new document was printed in September 2010. It summarises the current scientific evidence and highlights the areas where the science is well established, where there is still some debate, and where substantial uncertainties remain. The society has stated that "this is not the same as saying that the climate science itself is in error – no Fellows have expressed such a view to the RS".<sup id="cite_ref-RS-CC_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-CC-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>  The introduction includes this statement: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>There is strong evidence that the warming of the Earth over the last half-century has been caused largely by human activity, such as the burning of fossil fuels and changes in land use, including agriculture and deforestation.</p></blockquote></li></ul>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="International_science_academies">International science academies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: International science academies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/African_Academy_of_Sciences" title="African Academy of Sciences">African Academy of Sciences</a> in 2007 was a signatory to the "statement on sustainability, energy efficiency, and climate change". This joint statement of African science academies, was organized through the <a href="/wiki/Network_of_African_Science_Academies" title="Network of African Science Academies">Network of African Science Academies</a>. Its stated goal was "to convey information and spur action on the occasion of the G8 Summit in Heiligendamm, Germany, in June 2007". <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>A consensus, based on current evidence, now exists within the global scientific community that human activities are the main source of climate change and that the burning of fossil fuels is largely responsible for driving this change.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/European_Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts" title="European Academy of Sciences and Arts">European Academy of Sciences and Arts</a> in 2007 issued a formal declaration on climate change titled <i>Let's Be Honest</i>: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Human activity is most <i>likely</i> responsible for climate warming. Most of the climatic warming over the last 50 years is <i>likely</i> to have been caused by increased concentrations of greenhouse gases in the atmosphere. Documented long-term climate changes include changes in Arctic temperatures and ice, widespread changes in precipitation amounts, ocean salinity, wind patterns and <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> including droughts, heavy precipitation, heat waves and the intensity of tropical cyclones. The above development potentially has dramatic consequences for mankind's future.<sup id="cite_ref-euro-acad_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euro-acad-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/European_Science_Foundation" title="European Science Foundation">European Science Foundation</a> in a 2007 position paper <sup id="cite_ref-European_Science_Foundation_Position_Paper_&#39;&#39;Impacts_of_Climate_Change_on_the_European_Marine_and_Coastal_Environment_—_Ecosystems_Approach&#39;&#39;_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Science_Foundation_Position_Paper_&#39;&#39;Impacts_of_Climate_Change_on_the_European_Marine_and_Coastal_Environment_—_Ecosystems_Approach&#39;&#39;-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> states: <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>There is now convincing evidence that since the industrial revolution, human activities, resulting in increasing concentrations of greenhouse gases have become a major agent of climate change... On-going and increased efforts to mitigate climate change through reduction in greenhouse gases are therefore crucial.</p></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/InterAcademy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="InterAcademy Council">InterAcademy Council</a> As the representative of the world's <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy of Sciences">scientific and engineering academies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-interacademycouncil_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interacademycouncil-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> the InterAcademy Council issued a report in 2007 titled <i>Lighting the Way: Toward a Sustainable Energy Future</i>. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Current patterns of energy resources and energy usage are proving detrimental to the long-term welfare of humanity. The integrity of essential natural systems is already at risk from climate change caused by the atmospheric emissions of greenhouse gases.<sup id="cite_ref-interacademycouncil7_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interacademycouncil7-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Concerted efforts should be mounted for improving energy efficiency and reducing the carbon intensity of the world economy.<sup id="cite_ref-interacademycouncil8_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interacademycouncil8-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote></li></ul>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/International_Council_of_Academies_of_Engineering_and_Technological_Sciences" title="International Council of Academies of Engineering and Technological Sciences">International Council of Academies of Engineering and Technological Sciences</a> (CAETS) in 2007, issued a <i>Statement on Environment and Sustainable Growth</i>:<sup id="cite_ref-caets_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caets-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>As reported by the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC), most of the observed global warming since the mid-20th century is very likely due to human-produced emission of greenhouse gases and this warming will continue unabated if present anthropogenic emissions continue or, worse, expand without control. CAETS, therefore, endorses the many recent calls to decrease and control greenhouse gas emissions to an acceptable level as quickly as possible.</p></blockquote></li></ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_and_chemical_sciences">Physical and chemical sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Physical and chemical sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/American_Chemical_Society" title="American Chemical Society">American Chemical Society</a><sup id="cite_ref-American_Chemical_Society_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change&#39;&#39;_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_Chemical_Society_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change&#39;&#39;-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Physics" title="American Institute of Physics">American Institute of Physics</a><sup id="cite_ref-American_Institute_of_Physics_Statement_supporting_AGU_statement_on_human-induced_climate_change_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_Institute_of_Physics_Statement_supporting_AGU_statement_on_human-induced_climate_change-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Physical_Society" title="American Physical Society">American Physical Society</a><sup id="cite_ref-American_Physical_Society_Climate_Change_Policy_Statement_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_Physical_Society_Climate_Change_Policy_Statement-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Australian_Institute_of_Physics" title="Australian Institute of Physics">Australian Institute of Physics</a><sup id="cite_ref-AIP_science_policy_document._73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP_science_policy_document.-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Physical_Society" title="European Physical Society">European Physical Society</a><sup id="cite_ref-EPS_Position_Paper_&#39;&#39;Energy_for_the_future:_The_Nuclear_Option&#39;&#39;_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPS_Position_Paper_&#39;&#39;Energy_for_the_future:_The_Nuclear_Option&#39;&#39;-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_sciences">Earth sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Earth sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Geophysical_Union">American Geophysical Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: American Geophysical Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Geophysical_Union" title="American Geophysical Union">American Geophysical Union</a> (AGU) adopted a statement on <i>Climate Change and Greenhouse Gases</i> in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> A new statement, adopted by the society in 2003, revised in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-agu_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agu-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> and revised and expanded in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> affirms that rising levels of greenhouse gases have caused and will continue to cause the global surface temperature to be warmer:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Human activities are changing Earth's climate. At the global level, atmospheric concentrations of carbon dioxide and other heat-trapping greenhouse gases have increased sharply since the Industrial Revolution. Fossil fuel burning dominates this increase. Human-caused increases in greenhouse gases are responsible for most of the observed global average surface warming of roughly 0.8&#8239;°C (1.5&#8239;°F) over the past 140 years. Because natural processes cannot quickly remove some of these gases (notably carbon dioxide) from the atmosphere, our past, present, and future emissions will influence the climate system for millennia.
</p><p>While important scientific uncertainties remain as to which particular impacts will be experienced where, no uncertainties are known that could make the impacts of climate change inconsequential. Furthermore, surprise outcomes, such as the unexpectedly rapid loss of Arctic summer sea ice, may entail even more dramatic changes than anticipated.
</p>
</blockquote>
<h5><span id="American_Society_of_Agronomy.2C_Crop_Science_Society_of_America.2C_and_Soil_Science_Society_of_America"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Society_of_Agronomy,_Crop_Science_Society_of_America,_and_Soil_Science_Society_of_America">American Society of Agronomy, Crop Science Society of America, and Soil Science Society of America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: American Society of Agronomy, Crop Science Society of America, and Soil Science Society of America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In May, 2011, the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Agronomy" title="American Society of Agronomy">American Society of Agronomy</a> (ASA), Crop Science Society of America (CSSA), and <a href="/wiki/Soil_Science_Society_of_America" title="Soil Science Society of America">Soil Science Society of America</a> (SSSA) issued a joint position statement on climate change as it relates to agriculture:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>A comprehensive body of scientific evidence indicates beyond reasonable doubt that global climate change is now occurring and that its manifestations threaten the stability of societies as well as natural and managed ecosystems. Increases in ambient temperatures and changes in related processes are directly linked to rising anthropogenic greenhouse gas (GHG) concentrations in the atmosphere.
</p><p>Unless the emissions of GHGs are curbed significantly, their concentrations will continue to rise, leading to changes in temperature, precipitation, and other climate variables that will undoubtedly affect agriculture around the world.
</p><p>Climate change has the potential to increase weather variability as well as gradually increase global temperatures. Both of these impacts have the potential to negatively impact the adaptability and resilience of the world's food production capacity; current research indicates climate change is already reducing the productivity of vulnerable cropping systems.<sup id="cite_ref-soils_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soils-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Federation_of_Geologists">European Federation of Geologists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: European Federation of Geologists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 2008, the European Federation of Geologists<sup id="cite_ref-eurogeologists_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogeologists-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> (EFG) issued the position paper <i>Carbon Capture and geological Storage </i>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The EFG recognizes the work of the IPCC and other organizations, and subscribes to the major findings that climate change is happening, is predominantly caused by anthropogenic emissions of CO<sub>2</sub>, and poses a significant threat to human civilization.
</p><p>It is clear that major efforts are necessary to quickly and strongly reduce CO<sub>2</sub> emissions. The EFG strongly advocates renewable and sustainable energy production, including geothermal energy, as well as the need for increasing energy efficiency.
</p><p>CCS [Carbon Capture and geological Storage] should also be regarded as a bridging technology, facilitating the move towards a carbon free economy.<sup id="cite_ref-eurogeologists9_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogeologists9-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Geosciences_Union">European Geosciences Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: European Geosciences Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 2005, the Divisions of Atmospheric and Climate Sciences of the <a href="/wiki/European_Geosciences_Union" title="European Geosciences Union">European Geosciences Union</a> (EGU) issued a position statement in support of the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change#Joint_science_academies’_statement_2005" title="Scientific opinion on climate change">joint science academies’ statement</a> on global response to climate change. The statement refers to the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> (IPCC), as "the main representative of the global <a href="/wiki/Scientific_community" title="Scientific community">scientific community</a>", and asserts that the IPCC
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>represents the state-of-the-art of climate science supported by the major science academies around the world and by the vast majority of science researchers and investigators as documented by the <a href="/wiki/Peer-reviewed" class="mw-redirect" title="Peer-reviewed">peer-reviewed</a> scientific literature.<sup id="cite_ref-www_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Additionally, in 2008, the EGU issued a position statement on <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a> which states, "Ocean acidification is already occurring today and will continue to intensify, closely tracking <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_in_the_Earth%27s_atmosphere" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon dioxide in the Earth&#39;s atmosphere">atmospheric CO<sub>2</sub></a> increase. Given the potential threat to <a href="/wiki/Marine_ecosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine ecosystems">marine ecosystems</a> and its ensuing impact on human society and economy, especially as it acts in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Anthropogenic_global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropogenic global warming">anthropogenic global warming</a>, there is an urgent need for immediate action." The statement then advocates for strategies "to limit future release of CO<sub>2</sub> to the atmosphere and/or enhance removal of excess CO<sub>2</sub> from the atmosphere."<sup id="cite_ref-www10_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www10-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Geological_Society_of_America">Geological Society of America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Geological Society of America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Geological_Society_of_America" title="Geological Society of America">Geological Society of America</a> adopted a position statement on global <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. It amended this position on April 20, 2010 with more explicit comments on need for CO<sub>2</sub> reduction.
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Decades of scientific research have shown that climate can change from both natural and anthropogenic causes. The Geological Society of America (GSA) concurs with assessments by the National Academies of Science (2005), the National Research Council (2006), and the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC, 2007) that global climate has warmed and that human activities (mainly greenhouse‐gas emissions) account for most of the warming since the middle 1900s. If current trends continue, the projected increase in global temperature by the end of the twenty first century will result in large impacts on humans and other species. Addressing the challenges posed by climate change will require a combination of adaptation to the changes that are likely to occur and global reductions of CO<sub>2</sub> emissions from anthropogenic sources.<sup id="cite_ref-geosociety_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geosociety-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Geological_Society_of_London">Geological Society of London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Geological Society of London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In November 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Geological_Society_of_London" title="Geological Society of London">Geological Society of London</a> issued the position statement <i>Climate change: evidence from the geological record</i>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The last century has seen a rapidly growing global population and much more intensive use of resources, leading to greatly increased emissions of gases, such as carbon dioxide and methane, from the burning of fossil fuels (oil, gas and coal), and from agriculture, cement production and deforestation. Evidence from the geological record is consistent with the physics that shows that adding large amounts of carbon dioxide to the atmosphere warms the world and may lead to: higher sea levels and flooding of low-lying coasts; greatly changed patterns of rainfall; increased acidity of the oceans; and decreased oxygen levels in seawater.
</p><p>There is now widespread concern that the Earth's climate will warm further, not only because of the lingering effects of the added carbon already in the system, but also because of further additions as human population continues to grow. Life on Earth has survived large climate changes in the past, but extinctions and major redistribution of species have been associated with many of them. When the human population was small and nomadic, a rise in sea level of a few metres would have had very little effect on Homo sapiens. With the current and growing global population, much of which is concentrated in coastal cities, such a rise in sea level would have a drastic effect on our complex society, especially if the climate were to change as suddenly as it has at times in the past. Equally, it seems likely that as warming continues some areas may experience less precipitation leading to drought. With both rising seas and increasing drought, pressure for human migration could result on a large scale.<sup id="cite_ref-geolsoc_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geolsoc-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Union_of_Geodesy_and_Geophysics">International Union of Geodesy and Geophysics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: International Union of Geodesy and Geophysics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In July 2007, the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_of_Geodesy_and_Geophysics" title="International Union of Geodesy and Geophysics">International Union of Geodesy and Geophysics</a> (IUGG) adopted a resolution titled "The Urgency of Addressing Climate Change". In it, the IUGG concurs with the "comprehensive and widely accepted and endorsed scientific assessments carried out by the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change and regional and national bodies, which have firmly established, on the basis of scientific evidence, that human activities are the primary cause of recent climate change." They state further that the "continuing reliance on combustion of fossil fuels as the world's primary source of energy will lead to much higher atmospheric concentrations of greenhouse gases, which will, in turn, cause significant increases in surface temperature, sea level, ocean acidification, and their related consequences to the environment and society."<sup id="cite_ref-iugg_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iugg-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Association_of_Geoscience_Teachers">National Association of Geoscience Teachers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: National Association of Geoscience Teachers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In July 2009, the National Association of Geoscience Teachers<sup id="cite_ref-nagt_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nagt-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> (NAGT) adopted a position statement on climate change in which they assert that "Earth's climate is changing [and] "that present warming trends are largely the result of human activities":
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>NAGT strongly supports and will work to promote education in the science of climate change, the causes and effects of current global warming, and the immediate need for policies and actions that reduce the emission of greenhouse gases.<sup id="cite_ref-nagt11_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nagt11-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorology_and_oceanography">Meteorology and oceanography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Meteorology and oceanography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Meteorological_Society">American Meteorological Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: American Meteorological Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Meteorological_Society" title="American Meteorological Society">American Meteorological Society</a> (AMS) statement adopted by their council in 2012 concluded:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>There is unequivocal evidence that Earth's lower atmosphere, ocean, and land surface are warming; sea level is rising; and snow cover, mountain glaciers, and Arctic sea ice are shrinking.
