The dominant cause of the warming since the 1950s is human activities. This scientific finding is based on a large and persuasive body of research. The observed warming will be irreversible for many years into the future, and even larger temperature increases will occur as greenhouse gases continue to accumulate in the atmosphere. Avoiding this future warming will require a large and rapid reduction in global greenhouse gas emissions. The ongoing warming will increase risks and stresses to human societies, economies, ecosystems, and wildlife through the 21st century and beyond, making it imperative that society respond to a changing climate. To inform decisions on adaptation and mitigation, it is critical that we improve our understanding of the global climate system and our ability to project future climate through continued and improved monitoring and research. This is especially true for smaller (seasonal and regional) scales and weather and climate extremes, and for important hydroclimatic variables such as precipitation and water availability.
</p><p>Technological, economic, and policy choices in the near future will determine the extent of future impacts of climate change. Science-based decisions are seldom made in a context of absolute certainty. National and international policy discussions should include consideration of the best ways to both adapt to and mitigate climate change. Mitigation will reduce the amount of future climate change and the risk of impacts that are potentially large and dangerous. At the same time, some continued climate change is inevitable, and policy responses should include adaptation to climate change. Prudence dictates extreme care in accounting for our relationship with the only planet known to be capable of sustaining human life.<sup id="cite_ref-ametsoc_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ametsoc-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Australian_Meteorological_and_Oceanographic_Society">Australian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Australian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Meteorological_and_Oceanographic_Society" title="Australian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society">Australian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society</a> has issued a <i>Statement on Climate Change</i>, wherein they conclude:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Global climate change and global warming are real and observable ... It is highly likely that those human activities that have increased the concentration of greenhouse gases in the atmosphere have been largely responsible for the observed warming since 1950. The warming associated with increases in greenhouse gases originating from human activity is called the enhanced <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_effect" title="Greenhouse effect">greenhouse effect</a>. The atmospheric concentration of carbon dioxide has increased by more than 30% since the start of the industrial age and is higher now than at any time in at least the past 650,000 years. This increase is a direct result of burning fossil fuels, broad-scale <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> and other human activity."<sup id="cite_ref-amos_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amos-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Canadian_Foundation_for_Climate_and_Atmospheric_Sciences">Canadian Foundation for Climate and Atmospheric Sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Canadian Foundation for Climate and Atmospheric Sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In November 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Foundation_for_Climate_and_Atmospheric_Sciences" title="Canadian Foundation for Climate and Atmospheric Sciences">Canadian Foundation for Climate and Atmospheric Sciences</a> (CFCAS) issued a letter to the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister of Canada</a> stating that
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We concur with the climate science assessment of the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) in 2001 ... We endorse the conclusions of the IPCC assessment that 'There is new and stronger evidence that most of the warming observed over the last 50 years is attributable to human activities'. ... There is increasingly unambiguous evidence of changing climate in Canada and around the world. There will be increasing impacts of climate change on Canada's natural ecosystems and on our socio-economic activities. Advances in climate science since the 2001 IPCC Assessment have provided more evidence supporting the need for action and development of a strategy for adaptation to projected changes.<sup id="cite_ref-cfcas_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfcas-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Canadian_Meteorological_and_Oceanographic_Society">Canadian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Canadian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In November 2009,  a letter to the Canadian Parliament by The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Meteorological_and_Oceanographic_Society" title="Canadian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society">Canadian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society</a> states:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Rigorous international research, including work carried out and supported by the Government of Canada, reveals that greenhouse gases resulting from human activities contribute to the warming of the atmosphere and the oceans and constitute a serious risk to the health and safety of our society, as well as having an impact on all life.<sup id="cite_ref-cmos_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmos-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h5><span id="Royal_Meteorological_Society_.28UK.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Meteorological_Society_(UK)">Royal Meteorological Society (UK)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Royal Meteorological Society (UK)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In February 2007, after the release of the IPCC's Fourth Assessment Report, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Meteorological_Society" title="Royal Meteorological Society">Royal Meteorological Society</a> issued an endorsement of the report. In addition to referring to the IPCC as "[the] world's best climate scientists", they stated that climate change is happening as "the result of emissions since industrialization and we have already set in motion the next 50 years of global warming – what we do from now on will determine how worse it will get."<sup id="cite_ref-rmets_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rmets-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Meteorological_Organization">World Meteorological Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: World Meteorological Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In its <i>Statement at the Twelfth Session of the Conference of the Parties to the U.N. Framework Convention on Climate Change</i> presented on November 15, 2006, the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> (WMO) confirms the need to "<a href="/wiki/Avoiding_dangerous_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Avoiding dangerous climate change">prevent dangerous anthropogenic interference with the climate system</a>." The WMO concurs that "scientific assessments have increasingly reaffirmed that human activities are indeed changing the composition of the atmosphere, in particular through the burning of fossil fuels for energy production and transportation." The WMO concurs that "the present atmospheric concentration of CO<sub>2</sub> was never exceeded over the past 420,000 years;" and that the IPCC "assessments provide the most authoritative, up-to-date scientific advice."
<sup id="cite_ref-www12_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www12-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Quaternary_Association">American Quaternary Association</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: American Quaternary Association">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Quaternary_Association" title="American Quaternary Association">American Quaternary Association</a> (AMQUA) has stated
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Few credible Scientists now doubt that humans have influenced the documented rise of global temperatures since the Industrial Revolution," citing "the growing body of evidence that warming of the atmosphere, especially over the past 50 years, is directly impacted by human activity.<sup id="cite_ref-agu13_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agu13-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Union_for_Quaternary_Research">International Union for Quaternary Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: International Union for Quaternary Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The statement on climate change issued by the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Quaternary_Research" title="International Union for Quaternary Research">International Union for Quaternary Research</a> (INQUA) reiterates the conclusions of the IPCC, and urges all nations to take prompt action in line with the <a href="/wiki/UNFCCC" class="mw-redirect" title="UNFCCC">UNFCCC</a> principles.
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Human activities are now causing atmospheric concentrations of greenhouse gases — including carbon dioxide, methane, tropospheric ozone, and nitrous oxide — to rise well above pre-industrial levels….Increases in greenhouse gases are causing temperatures to rise…The scientific understanding of climate change is now sufficiently clear to justify nations taking prompt action….Minimizing the amount of this carbon dioxide reaching the atmosphere presents a huge challenge but must be a global priority.<sup id="cite_ref-inqua_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inqua-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Biology_and_life_sciences">Biology and life sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Biology and life sciences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Life science organizations have outlined the dangers climate change pose to wildlife.
</p>
<ul><li>American Association of Wildlife Veterinarians<sup id="cite_ref-AAWV_&#39;&#39;Position_Statement_on_Climate_Change,_Wildlife_Diseases,_and_Wildlife_Health&#39;&#39;_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAWV_&#39;&#39;Position_Statement_on_Climate_Change,_Wildlife_Diseases,_and_Wildlife_Health&#39;&#39;-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Biological_Sciences" title="American Institute of Biological Sciences">American Institute of Biological Sciences</a>. In October 2009, the leaders of 18 US scientific societies and organizations sent an open letter to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> reaffirming the scientific consensus that climate change is occurring and is primarily caused by human activities.  The American Institute of Biological Sciences (AIBS) adopted this letter as their official position statement.<sup id="cite_ref-AIBS_Position_Statements_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIBS_Position_Statements-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Scientific_societies_warn_Senate:_climate_change_is_real_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scientific_societies_warn_Senate:_climate_change_is_real-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The letter goes on to warn of predicted impacts on the United States such as <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a> and increases in <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather_events" class="mw-redirect" title="Extreme weather events">extreme weather events</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_scarcity" title="Water scarcity">water scarcity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heat_waves" class="mw-redirect" title="Heat waves">heat waves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wildfires" class="mw-redirect" title="Wildfires">wildfires</a>, and the disturbance of <a href="/wiki/Biological_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Biological systems">biological systems</a>.  It then advocates for a dramatic reduction in emissions of greenhouse gases.<sup id="cite_ref-Letter_to_US_Senators_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Letter_to_US_Senators-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Society_for_Microbiology" title="American Society for Microbiology">American Society for Microbiology</a><sup id="cite_ref-Global_Environmental_Change_—_Microbial_Contributions,_Microbial_Solutions_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Environmental_Change_—_Microbial_Contributions,_Microbial_Solutions-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Australian Coral Reef Society<sup id="cite_ref-Australian_Coral_Reef_Society_official_letter_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Australian_Coral_Reef_Society_official_letter-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Biology" title="Institute of Biology">Institute of Biology</a> (UK)<sup id="cite_ref-iob_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iob-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Society_of_American_Foresters" title="Society of American Foresters">Society of American Foresters</a> issued two position statements pertaining to climate change in which they cite the IPCC<sup id="cite_ref-SAF_&#39;&#39;Forest_Management_and_Climate_Change_&#39;&#39;_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAF_&#39;&#39;Forest_Management_and_Climate_Change_&#39;&#39;-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> and the UNFCCC.<sup id="cite_ref-SAF_&#39;&#39;Forest_Offset_Projects_in_a_Carbon_Trading_System&#39;&#39;_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAF_&#39;&#39;Forest_Offset_Projects_in_a_Carbon_Trading_System&#39;&#39;-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Wildlife_Society" title="The Wildlife Society">The Wildlife Society</a> (international)<sup id="cite_ref-Wildlife_Society_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change_and_Wildlife&#39;&#39;_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wildlife_Society_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change_and_Wildlife&#39;&#39;-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_health">Human health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Human health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A number of health organizations have warned about the numerous <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming_on_human_health" title="Effects of global warming on human health">negative health effects of global warming</a>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Pediatrics" title="American Academy of Pediatrics">American Academy of Pediatrics</a><sup id="cite_ref-AAP_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change_and_Children&#39;s_Health&#39;&#39;_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAP_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change_and_Children&#39;s_Health&#39;&#39;-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_College_of_Preventive_Medicine" title="American College of Preventive Medicine">American College of Preventive Medicine</a><sup id="cite_ref-ACPM_Policy_Statement_&#39;&#39;Abrupt_Climate_Change_and_Public_Health_Implications&#39;&#39;_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACPM_Policy_Statement_&#39;&#39;Abrupt_Climate_Change_and_Public_Health_Implications&#39;&#39;-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Association" title="American Medical Association">American Medical Association</a><sup id="cite_ref-American_Medical_Association_Policy_Statement_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_Medical_Association_Policy_Statement-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Public_Health_Association" title="American Public Health Association">American Public Health Association</a><sup id="cite_ref-apha_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apha-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Australian_Medical_Association" title="Australian Medical Association">Australian Medical Association</a> in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-AMA_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_Human_Health_—_2004&#39;&#39;_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMA_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_Human_Health_—_2004&#39;&#39;-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and in 2008<sup id="cite_ref-AMA_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_Human_Health&#39;&#39;_—_2004._Revised_2008._111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMA_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_Human_Health&#39;&#39;_—_2004._Revised_2008.-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>World Federation of Public Health Associations<sup id="cite_ref-wfpha_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wfpha-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a><sup id="cite_ref-WHO_&#39;&#39;Protecting_health_from_climate_change&#39;&#39;_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_&#39;&#39;Protecting_health_from_climate_change&#39;&#39;-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>There is now widespread agreement that the Earth is warming, due to emissions of greenhouse gases caused by human activity. It is also clear that current trends in energy use, development, and population growth will lead to continuing – and more severe – climate change.
</p></blockquote>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The changing climate will inevitably affect the basic requirements for maintaining health: clean air and water, sufficient food and adequate shelter. Each year, about 800,000 people die from causes attributable to <a href="/wiki/Urban_air_pollution" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban air pollution">urban air pollution</a>, 1.8 million from <a href="/wiki/Diarrhoea" class="mw-redirect" title="Diarrhoea">diarrhoea</a> resulting from lack of access to clean water supply, sanitation, and poor hygiene, 3.5 million from <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> and approximately 60,000 in natural disasters. A warmer and more variable climate threatens to lead to higher levels of some air pollutants, increase transmission of diseases through unclean water and through contaminated food, to compromise agricultural production in some of the least developed countries, and increase the hazards of extreme weather.
</p></blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Miscellaneous">Miscellaneous</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Miscellaneous">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A number of other national scientific societies have also endorsed the opinion of the IPCC:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/American_Astronomical_Society" title="American Astronomical Society">American Astronomical Society</a><sup id="cite_ref-Statement_supporting_AGU_statement_on_human-induced_climate_change_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statement_supporting_AGU_statement_on_human-induced_climate_change-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Statistical_Association" title="American Statistical Association">American Statistical Association</a><sup id="cite_ref-ASA_Statement_on_Climate_Change_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASA_Statement_on_Climate_Change-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canadian_Council_of_Professional_Engineers" title="Canadian Council of Professional Engineers">Canadian Council of Professional Engineers</a>  <sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Institution of <a href="/wiki/Engineers_Australia" title="Engineers Australia">Engineers Australia</a><sup id="cite_ref-Policy_Statement,_Climate_Change_and_Energy_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Policy_Statement,_Climate_Change_and_Energy-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>International Association for Great Lakes Research<sup id="cite_ref-IAGLR_Fact_Sheet_&#39;&#39;The_Great_Lakes_at_a_Crossroads:_Preparing_for_a_Changing_Climate&#39;&#39;_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAGLR_Fact_Sheet_&#39;&#39;The_Great_Lakes_at_a_Crossroads:_Preparing_for_a_Changing_Climate&#39;&#39;-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Institute of Professional Engineers New Zealand<sup id="cite_ref-IPENZ_Informatory_Note,_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_the_greenhouse_effect&#39;&#39;_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPENZ_Informatory_Note,_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_the_greenhouse_effect&#39;&#39;-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wfeo.net/events/international-conclave-on-climate-change/%20%20">The World Federation of Engineering Organizations (WFEO)</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-committal">Non-committal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Non-committal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="Non-committal_statements"></span>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Association_of_Petroleum_Geologists">American Association of Petroleum Geologists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: American Association of Petroleum Geologists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of June 2007, the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Petroleum_Geologists" title="American Association of Petroleum Geologists">American Association of Petroleum Geologists</a> (AAPG) Position Statement on climate change stated:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>the AAPG membership is divided on the degree of influence that anthropogenic CO<sub>2</sub> has on recent and potential global temperature increases ... Certain climate simulation models predict that the warming trend will continue, as reported through NAS, AGU, AAAS and AMS. AAPG respects these scientific opinions but wants to add that the current climate warming projections could fall within well-documented natural variations in past climate and observed temperature data. These data do not necessarily support the maximum case scenarios forecast in some models.<sup id="cite_ref-aapg_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aapg-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Prior to the adoption of this statement, the AAPG was the only major scientific organization that rejected the finding of significant human influence on recent climate, according to a statement by the Council of the American Quaternary Association.<sup id="cite_ref-AQAonAAPG_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AQAonAAPG-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Explaining the plan for a revision, AAPG president Lee Billingsly wrote in March 2007:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Members have threatened to not renew their memberships… if AAPG does not alter its position on global climate change... And I have been told of members who already have resigned in previous years because of our current global climate change position… The current policy statement is not supported by a significant number of our members and prospective members.<sup id="cite_ref-aapg14_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aapg14-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>AAPG President John Lorenz announced the "sunsetting" of AAPG's Global Climate Change Committee in January 2010.  The AAPG Executive Committee determined:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Climate change is peripheral at best to our science […] AAPG does not have credibility in that field […] and as a group we have no particular knowledge of global atmospheric geophysics.<sup id="cite_ref-2010_tpgmarapr_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_tpgmarapr-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h4><span id="American_Institute_of_Professional_Geologists_.28AIPG.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Institute_of_Professional_Geologists_(AIPG)">American Institute of Professional Geologists (AIPG)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: American Institute of Professional Geologists (AIPG)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The official position statement from AIPG on the Environment states that "combustion of fossil fuel include and the generation of GHGs [greenhouse gases] including carbon dioxide (CO2) and methane (CH4).  Emissions of GHGs are perceived by some to be one of the largest, global environmental concerns related to energy production due to potential effects on the global energy system and possibly global climate. Fossil fuel use is the primary source of the increased atmospheric concentration of GHGs since industrialization".<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2010, AIPG's Executive Director issued a statement regarding polarization of opinions on climate change within the membership and announced that the AIPG Executive had made a decision to cease publication of articles and opinion pieces concerning climate change in AIPG's news journal, <i>The Professional Geologist</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-aipg17_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aipg17-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposing">Opposing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Opposing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_scientists_opposing_the_mainstream_scientific_assessment_of_global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="List of scientists opposing the mainstream scientific assessment of global warming">List of scientists opposing the mainstream scientific assessment of global warming</a></div>
<p>Since 2007, when the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Petroleum_Geologists" title="American Association of Petroleum Geologists">American Association of Petroleum Geologists</a> released a revised statement,<sup id="cite_ref-aapg19_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aapg19-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> no national or international scientific body rejects the findings of human-induced effects on climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-AQAonAAPG_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AQAonAAPG-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oreskes07p68_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oreskes07p68-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Surveys_of_scientists_and_scientific_literature">Surveys of scientists and scientific literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Surveys of scientists and scientific literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Surveys_of_scientists%27_views_on_climate_change" title="Surveys of scientists&#39; views on climate change">Surveys of scientists' views on climate change</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Climate_science_opinion2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Climate_science_opinion2.png/220px-Climate_science_opinion2.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Climate_science_opinion2.png/330px-Climate_science_opinion2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Climate_science_opinion2.png/440px-Climate_science_opinion2.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="606" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Climate_science_opinion2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Summary of opinions from climate and earth scientists regarding climate change. <a href="/wiki/File:Climate_science_opinion2.png" title="File:Climate science opinion2.png">Click</a> to see a more detailed summary of the sources.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cook_et_al._(2016)_Studies_consensus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Cook_et_al._%282016%29_Studies_consensus.jpg/220px-Cook_et_al._%282016%29_Studies_consensus.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Cook_et_al._%282016%29_Studies_consensus.jpg/330px-Cook_et_al._%282016%29_Studies_consensus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Cook_et_al._%282016%29_Studies_consensus.jpg/440px-Cook_et_al._%282016%29_Studies_consensus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cook_et_al._(2016)_Studies_consensus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seven papers into man-made global warming consensus, from 2004–2015, by <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Oreskes" title="Naomi Oreskes">Naomi Oreskes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Beyond_the_Ivory_Tower:_The_Scientific_Consensus_on_Climate_Change_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beyond_the_Ivory_Tower:_The_Scientific_Consensus_on_Climate_Change-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Doran" title="Peter Doran">Peter Doran</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-DZ_EOS_2009_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DZ_EOS_2009-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> William Anderegg,<sup id="cite_ref-Expert_credibility_in_climate_change_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Expert_credibility_in_climate_change-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Bart Verheggen,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Neil Stenhouse,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> J. Stuart Carlton,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> and John Cook.<sup id="cite_ref-Cook_etal_13_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cook_etal_13-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cook_etal_2016_05_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cook_etal_2016_05-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Various surveys have been conducted to evaluate scientific opinion on <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>. They have concluded that the majority of scientists support the idea of anthropogenic climate change.
</p><p>In 2004, the geologist and historian of science <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Oreskes" title="Naomi Oreskes">Naomi Oreskes</a> summarized a study of the scientific literature on climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-Beyond_the_Ivory_Tower:_The_Scientific_Consensus_on_Climate_Change_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beyond_the_Ivory_Tower:_The_Scientific_Consensus_on_Climate_Change-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> She analyzed 928 <a href="/wiki/Abstract_(summary)" title="Abstract (summary)">abstracts</a> of papers from refereed scientific journals between 1993 and 2003 and concluded that there is a scientific consensus on the reality of <a href="/wiki/Anthropogenic_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropogenic climate change">anthropogenic climate change</a>.
</p><p>Oreskes divided the abstracts into six categories: explicit endorsement of the consensus position, evaluation of impacts, mitigation proposals, methods, <a href="/wiki/Paleoclimatology" title="Paleoclimatology">paleoclimate</a> analysis, and rejection of the consensus position. Seventy-five per cent of the abstracts were placed in the first three categories (either explicitly or implicitly accepting the consensus view); 25% dealt with methods or paleoclimate, thus taking no position on current anthropogenic climate change. None of the abstracts disagreed with the consensus position, which the author found to be "remarkable". According to the report, "authors evaluating impacts, developing methods, or studying paleoclimatic change might believe that current climate change is natural. However, none of these papers argued that point."
</p><p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Harris_Interactive" title="Harris Interactive">Harris Interactive</a> surveyed 489 randomly selected members of either the <a href="/wiki/American_Meteorological_Society" title="American Meteorological Society">American Meteorological Society</a> or the <a href="/wiki/American_Geophysical_Union" title="American Geophysical Union">American Geophysical Union</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Statistical_Assessment_Service" title="Statistical Assessment Service">Statistical Assessment Service</a> (STATS) at <a href="/wiki/George_Mason_University" title="George Mason University">George Mason University</a>. 97% of the scientists surveyed agreed that global temperatures had increased during the past 100 years; 84% said they personally believed human-induced warming was occurring, and 74% agreed that "currently available scientific evidence" substantiated its occurrence. Catastrophic effects in 50–100 years would likely be observed according to 41%, while 44% thought the effects would be moderate and about 13 percent saw relatively little danger. 5% said they thought human activity did not contribute to greenhouse warming.<sup id="cite_ref-Survey_Tracks_Scientists&#39;_Growing_Climate_Concern_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Survey_Tracks_Scientists&#39;_Growing_Climate_Concern-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Climate_Scientists_Agree_on_Warming,_Disagree_on_Dangers,_and_Don&#39;t_Trust_the_Media&#39;s_Coverage_of_Climate_Change_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_Scientists_Agree_on_Warming,_Disagree_on_Dangers,_and_Don&#39;t_Trust_the_Media&#39;s_Coverage_of_Climate_Change-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-journalistsresource_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalistsresource-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Structure_of_Scientific_Opinion_on_Climate_Change_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Structure_of_Scientific_Opinion_on_Climate_Change-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dennis Bray and <a href="/wiki/Hans_von_Storch" title="Hans von Storch">Hans von Storch</a> conducted a survey in August 2008 of 2058 climate scientists from 34 different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Survey_of_the_Perspectives_of_Climate_Scientists_Concerning_Climate_Science_and_Climate_Change_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Survey_of_the_Perspectives_of_Climate_Scientists_Concerning_Climate_Science_and_Climate_Change-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> A web link with a unique identifier was given to each respondent to eliminate multiple responses. A total of 373 responses were received giving an overall response rate of 18.2%. No paper on climate change consensus based on this survey has been published yet (February 2010), but one on another subject has been published based on the survey.<sup id="cite_ref-Prediction&#39;_or_&#39;Projection;_The_nomenclature_of_climate_science_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prediction&#39;_or_&#39;Projection;_The_nomenclature_of_climate_science-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The survey was composed of 76 questions split into a number of sections.
There were sections on the demographics of the respondents, their assessment of the state of climate science, how good the science is, climate change impacts, adaptation and mitigation, their opinion of the IPCC, and how well climate science was being communicated to the public.
Most of the answers were on a scale from 1 to 7 from 'not at all' to 'very much'.
</p><p>To the question "How convinced are you that climate change, whether natural or anthropogenic, is occurring now?", 67.1% said they very much agreed, 26.7% agreed to some large extent, 6.2% said to they agreed to some small extent (2–4), none said they did not agree at all. To the question "How convinced are you that most of recent or near future climate change is, or will
be, a result of anthropogenic causes?" the responses were 34.6% very much agree, 48.9% agreeing to a large extent, 15.1% to a small extent, and 1.35% not agreeing at all.
</p><p>A poll performed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Doran" title="Peter Doran">Peter Doran</a> and Maggie Kendall Zimmerman at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Chicago" title="University of Illinois at Chicago">University of Illinois at Chicago</a> received replies from 3,146 of the 10,257 polled Earth scientists. Results were analyzed globally and by specialization. 76 out of 79 <a href="/wiki/Climatologists" class="mw-redirect" title="Climatologists">climatologists</a> who "listed climate science as their area of expertise and who also have published more than 50% of their recent peer-reviewed papers on the subject of climate change" believed that mean global temperatures had risen compared to pre-1800s levels. Seventy-five of 77 believed that human activity is a significant factor in changing mean global temperatures. Among all respondents, 90% agreed that temperatures have risen compared to pre-1800 levels, and 82% agreed that humans significantly influence the global temperature. <a href="/wiki/Economic_geologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic geologist">Economic geologists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meteorologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Meteorologist">meteorologists</a> were among the biggest doubters, with only 47 percent and 64 percent, respectively, believing in significant human involvement. The authors summarised the findings:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It seems that the debate on the authenticity of global warming and the role played by human activity is largely nonexistent among those who understand the nuances and scientific basis of long-term climate processes.<sup id="cite_ref-DZ_EOS_2009_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DZ_EOS_2009-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>A 2010 paper in the <a href="/wiki/Proceedings_of_the_National_Academy_of_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences"><i>Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States</i></a> (PNAS) reviewed publication and citation data for 1,372 climate researchers and drew the following two conclusions:
</p>
<blockquote><p>(i) 97–98% of the climate researchers most actively publishing in the field support the tenets of ACC (Anthropogenic Climate Change) outlined by the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change, and (ii) the relative climate expertise and scientific prominence of the researchers unconvinced of ACC are substantially below that of the convinced researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-Expert_credibility_in_climate_change_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Expert_credibility_in_climate_change-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>A 2013 paper in <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Research_Letters" title="Environmental Research Letters">Environmental Research Letters</a> reviewed 11,944 abstracts of scientific papers matching "global warming" or "global climate change". They found 4,014 which discussed the cause of recent global warming, and of these "97.1% endorsed the consensus position that humans are causing global warming".<sup id="cite_ref-Cook_etal_13_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cook_etal_13-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> This study was criticised by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Tol" title="Richard Tol">Richard Tol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tol_p=048001_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tol_p=048001-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/James_L._Powell" title="James L. Powell">James L. Powell</a>, a former member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Board" title="National Science Board">National Science Board</a> and current executive director of the <a href="/wiki/National_Physical_Science_Consortium" title="National Physical Science Consortium">National Physical Science Consortium</a>, analyzed published research on global warming and climate change between 1991 and 2012 and found that of the 13,950 articles in peer-reviewed journals, only 24 rejected anthropogenic global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> A follow-up analysis looking at 2,258 peer-reviewed climate articles with 9,136 authors published between November 2012 and December 2013 revealed that only one of the 9,136 authors rejected anthropogenic global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> His 2015 paper on the topic, covering 24,210 articles published by 69,406 authors during 2013 and 2014 found only five articles by four authors rejecting anthropogenic global warming. Over 99.99% of climate scientists did not reject AGW in their peer-reviewed research.<sup id="cite_ref-Powell2015_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powell2015-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Consensus_on_Anthropogenic_Global_Warming,_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/The_Consensus_on_Anthropogenic_Global_Warming%2C_2017.jpg/220px-The_Consensus_on_Anthropogenic_Global_Warming%2C_2017.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/The_Consensus_on_Anthropogenic_Global_Warming%2C_2017.jpg/330px-The_Consensus_on_Anthropogenic_Global_Warming%2C_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/The_Consensus_on_Anthropogenic_Global_Warming%2C_2017.jpg/440px-The_Consensus_on_Anthropogenic_Global_Warming%2C_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Consensus_on_Anthropogenic_Global_Warming,_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Peer-reviewed studies of the consensus on anthropogenic global warming.</div></div></div>
<p>In his latest paper, Powell reported that using rejection as the criterion of consensus, five surveys of the peer-reviewed literature from 1991 to 2015, including several of those above, combine to 54,195 articles with an average consensus of 99.94%.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Replication studies have shown that the 2% of climate science papers that rejected the scientific consensus on climate change in 2016 were methodologically flawed.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Existence_of_a_scientific_consensus">Existence of a scientific consensus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Existence of a scientific consensus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Scientific_consensus" title="Scientific consensus">Scientific consensus</a></div>
<p>A question that frequently arises in popular discussion of climate change is whether there is a scientific consensus on climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-Oreskes_consensus_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oreskes_consensus-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>  Several scientific organizations have explicitly used the term "consensus" in their statements:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">American Association for the Advancement of Science</a>, 2006: "The conclusions in this statement reflect the scientific consensus represented by, for example, the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change, and the Joint National Academies' statement."<sup id="cite_ref-aaas_board_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaas_board-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Academy of Sciences">US National Academy of Sciences</a>: "In the judgment of most climate scientists, Earth's warming in recent decades has been caused primarily by human activities that have increased the amount of greenhouse gases in the atmosphere. ... On climate change, [the National Academies’ reports] have assessed consensus findings on the science..."<sup id="cite_ref-nas_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nas-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Joint Science Academies' statement, 2005: "We recognise the international scientific consensus of the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC)."<sup id="cite_ref-nationalacademies21_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalacademies21-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Joint Science Academies' statement, 2001: "The work of the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) represents the consensus of the international scientific community on climate change science. We recognise IPCC as the world's most reliable source of information on climate change and its causes, and we endorse its method of achieving this consensus."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Science_of_Climate_Change_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Science_of_Climate_Change-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/American_Meteorological_Society" title="American Meteorological Society">American Meteorological Society</a>, 2003: "The nature of science is such that there is rarely total agreement among scientists. Individual scientific statements and papers—the validity of some of which has yet to be assessed adequately—can be exploited in the policy debate and can leave the impression that the scientific community is sharply divided on issues where there is, in reality, a strong scientific consensus.... IPCC assessment reports are prepared at approximately five-year intervals by a large international group of experts who represent the broad range of expertise and perspectives relevant to the issues. The reports strive to reflect a consensus evaluation of the results of the full body of peer-reviewed research.... They provide an analysis of what is known and not known, the degree of consensus, and some indication of the degree of confidence that can be placed on the various statements and conclusions."<sup id="cite_ref-ametsoc22_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ametsoc22-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Network_of_African_Science_Academies" title="Network of African Science Academies">Network of African Science Academies</a>: "A consensus, based on current evidence, now exists within the global scientific community that human activities are the main source of climate change and that the burning of fossil fuels is largely responsible for driving this change."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Quaternary_Research" title="International Union for Quaternary Research">International Union for Quaternary Research</a>, 2008: "INQUA recognizes the international scientific consensus of the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC)."<sup id="cite_ref-inqua_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inqua-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Australian Coral Reef Society,<sup id="cite_ref-australiancoralreefsociety_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-australiancoralreefsociety-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> 2006: "There is almost total consensus among experts that the earth's climate is changing as a result of the build-up of greenhouse gases.... There is broad scientific consensus that coral reefs are heavily affected by the activities of man and there are significant global influences that can make reefs more vulnerable such as global warming...."<sup id="cite_ref-australiancoralreefsociety24_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-australiancoralreefsociety24-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://climate.nasa.gov/scientific-consensus/">"Scientific consensus: Earth's climate is warming"</a>. <i>Climate Change: Vital Signs of the Planet</i>. National Aeronautics and Space Administration (NASA)<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2018-08-18</span></span>. <q>Multiple studies published in peer-reviewed scientific journals1 show that 97 percent or more of actively publishing climate scientists agree: Climate-warming trends over the past century are extremely likely due to human activities. In addition, most of the leading scientific organizations worldwide have issued public statements endorsing this position.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Climate+Change%3A+Vital+Signs+of+the+Planet&amp;rft.atitle=Scientific+consensus%3A+Earth%27s+climate+is+warming&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fclimate.nasa.gov%2Fscientific-consensus%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-AR4-warming-unequivocal-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AR4-warming-unequivocal_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Warming of the climate system is unequivocal, as is now evident from observations of increases in global average air and ocean temperatures, widespread melting of snow and ice and rising global average sea level." IPCC, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ipcc.ch/publications_and_data/ar4/syr/en/main.html">Synthesis Report</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ipcc.ch/publications_and_data/ar4/syr/en/mains1.html">Section 1.1: Observations of climate change</a>, in <a href="#CITEREFIPCC_AR4_SYR2007">IPCC AR4 SYR 2007</a>.</span>

<li id="cite_note-ipcc-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ipcc_7-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFIPCC" class="citation">IPCC, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ipcc.ch/pdf/assessment-report/ar5/wg1/WG1AR5_SPM_FINAL.pdf">"Summary for Policymakers"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, <i>Detection and Attribution of Climate Change</i>, <q>«It is extremely likely that human influence has been the dominant cause of the observed warming since the mid-20th century» (page 17) and «In this Summary for Policymakers, the following terms have been used to indicate the assessed likelihood of an outcome or a result: (...) extremely likely: 95–100%» (page 2).</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Summary+for+Policymakers&amp;rft.btitle=Detection+and+Attribution+of+Climate+Change&amp;rft.au=IPCC&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ipcc.ch%2Fpdf%2Fassessment-report%2Far5%2Fwg1%2FWG1AR5_SPM_FINAL.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/>, in <a href="#CITEREFIPCC_AR5_WG12013">IPCC AR5 WG1 2013</a>.</span>

<li id="cite_note-AmericasClimateChoices-2010-SciPanel-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AmericasClimateChoices-2010-SciPanel_9-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">[Notes-SciPanel] <cite class="citation book">America's Climate Choices: Panel on Advancing the Science of Climate Change; National Research Council (2010). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140529161102/http://www.nap.edu/catalog.php?record_id=12782"><i>Advancing the Science of Climate Change</i></a>. Washington, D.C.: The National Academies Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-309-14588-0" title="Special:BookSources/0-309-14588-0">0-309-14588-0</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nap.edu/catalog.php?record_id=12782">the original</a> on 2014-05-29. <q>(p1) ... there is a strong, credible body of evidence, based on multiple lines of research, documenting that climate is changing and that these changes are in large part caused by human activities. While much remains to be learned, the core phenomenon, scientific questions, and hypotheses have been examined thoroughly and have stood firm in the face of serious scientific debate and careful evaluation of alternative explanations. * * * (p21-22) Some scientific conclusions or theories have been so thoroughly examined and tested, and supported by so many independent observations and results, that their likelihood of subsequently being found to be wrong is vanishingly small. Such conclusions and theories are then regarded as settled facts. This is the case for the conclusions that the Earth system is warming and that much of this warming is very likely due to human activities.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Advancing+the+Science+of+Climate+Change&amp;rft.place=Washington%2C+D.C.&amp;rft.pub=The+National+Academies+Press&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=0-309-14588-0&amp;rft.au=America%27s+Climate+Choices%3A+Panel+on+Advancing+the+Science+of+Climate+Change%3B+National+Research+Council&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.nap.edu%2Fcatalog.php%3Frecord_id%3D12782&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-On_the_Climate_Change_Beat,_Doubt_Gives_Way_to_Certainty-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-On_the_Climate_Change_Beat,_Doubt_Gives_Way_to_Certainty_37-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Stevens, William K. (2007-02-06). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2007/02/06/science/earth/06clim.html?pagewanted=1&amp;ei=5088&amp;en=53862c0cdf77d1c0&amp;ex=1328418000&amp;partner=rssnyt&amp;emc=rss">"On the Climate Change Beat, Doubt Gives Way to Certainty"</a>. <i>New York Times</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2010-08-28</span></span>. <q>The Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change said the likelihood was 90 percent to 99 percent that emissions of heat-trapping greenhouse gases like carbon dioxide, spewed from tailpipes and smokestacks, were the dominant cause of the observed warming of the last 50 years. In the panel's parlance, this level of certainty is labeled "very likely." Only rarely does scientific odds-making provide a more definite answer than that, at least in this branch of science, and it describes the endpoint, so far, of a progression.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=New+York+Times&amp;rft.atitle=On+the+Climate+Change+Beat%2C+Doubt+Gives+Way+to+Certainty&amp;rft.date=2007-02-06&amp;rft.aulast=Stevens&amp;rft.aufirst=William+K.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nytimes.com%2F2007%2F02%2F06%2Fscience%2Fearth%2F06clim.html%3Fpagewanted%3D1%26ei%3D5088%26en%3D53862c0cdf77d1c0%26ex%3D1328418000%26partner%3Drssnyt%26emc%3Drss&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-Stanowisko_Zgromadzenia_Ogólnego_PAN_z_dnia_13_grudnia_2007_r-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Stanowisko_Zgromadzenia_Ogólnego_PAN_z_dnia_13_grudnia_2007_r_53-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aktualnosci.pan.pl/images/stories/pliki/stanowiska_opinie/2008/stanowisko_pan_131207.pdf">"Stanowisko Zgromadzenia Ogólnego PAN z dnia 13 grudnia 2007 r"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> (in Polish). Polish Academy of Sciences<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2009-06-16</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Stanowisko+Zgromadzenia+Og%C3%B3lnego+PAN+z+dnia+13+grudnia+2007+r&amp;rft.pub=Polish+Academy+of+Sciences&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aktualnosci.pan.pl%2Fimages%2Fstories%2Fpliki%2Fstanowiska_opinie%2F2008%2Fstanowisko_pan_131207.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> <i>Note</i>: As of 16 June 2009, PAS has not issued this statement in English, all citations have been translated from Polish.</span>

<li id="cite_note-aaas_board-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-aaas_board_54-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-aaas_board_54-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aaas.org/sites/default/files/migrate/uploads/aaas_climate_statement1.pdf">AAAS Board Statement on Climate Change</a> <i>www.aaas.org</i> December 2006</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FASTS_Statement_on_Climate_Change-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FASTS_Statement_on_Climate_Change_55-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fasts.org/images/policy-discussion/statement-climate-change.pdf"><i>FASTS Statement on Climate Change</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, 2008</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=FASTS+Statement+on+Climate+Change&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.fasts.org%2Fimages%2Fpolicy-discussion%2Fstatement-climate-change.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Global climate change is real and measurable. Since the start of the 20th century, the global mean surface temperature of the Earth has increased by more than 0.7°C and the rate of warming has been largest in the last 30 years.  Key vulnerabilities arising from climate change include water resources, food supply, health, coastal settlements, biodiversity and some key <a href="/wiki/Ecosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecosystems">ecosystems</a> such as coral reefs and alpine regions. As the atmospheric concentration of greenhouse gases increases, impacts become more severe and widespread. To reduce the global net economic, environmental and social losses in the face of these impacts, the policy objective must remain squarely focused on returning greenhouse gas concentrations to near pre-industrial levels through the reduction of emissions.  The spatial and temporal fingerprint of warming can be traced to increasing greenhouse gas concentrations in the atmosphere, which are a direct result of burning fossil fuels, broad-scale deforestation and other human activity."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-CCSAASKQ-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-CCSAASKQ_56-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CCSAASKQ_56-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Committee on the Science of Climate Change, Division on Earth and Life Studies, National Research Council (2001). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20010628070322/http://books.nap.edu/html/climatechange/"><i>Climate Change Science: An Analysis of Some Key Questions</i></a>. Washington DC: National Academy Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-309-07574-2" title="Special:BookSources/0-309-07574-2">0-309-07574-2</a>. <li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.interacademies.net/file.aspx?id=4825">"Joint statement by the Network of African Science Academies (NASAC) to the G8 on sustainability,  energy efficiency and climate change"</a>. 2007<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">22 May</span> 2015</span>. <q>A consensus, based on current evidence, now exists within the global scientific community that human activities are the main source of climate change and that the burning of fossil fuels is largely responsible for driving this change... Although we recognize that this nexus poses daunting challenges for the developed world, we firmly believe that these challenges are even more daunting for the most impoverished, science-poor regions of the developing world, especially in Africa.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Joint+statement+by+the+Network+of+African+Science+Academies+%28NASAC%29+to+the+G8+on+sustainability%2C++energy+efficiency+and+climate+change&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.interacademies.net%2Ffile.aspx%3Fid%3D4825&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-euro-acad-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-euro-acad_63-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.euro-acad.eu/downloads/memorandas/lets_be_honest_-_festplenum_03.03.07_-_final2.pdf">European Academy of Sciences and Arts <i>Let's Be Honest</i></a></span>

<li id="cite_note-European_Science_Foundation_Position_Paper_&#39;&#39;Impacts_of_Climate_Change_on_the_European_Marine_and_Coastal_Environment_—_Ecosystems_Approach&#39;&#39;-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-European_Science_Foundation_Position_Paper_&#39;&#39;Impacts_of_Climate_Change_on_the_European_Marine_and_Coastal_Environment_—_Ecosystems_Approach&#39;&#39;_64-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.esf.org/publications/position-papers.html"><i>European Science Foundation Position Paper </i>Impacts of Climate Change on the European Marine and Coastal Environment — Ecosystems Approach<i><span></span></i></a>, 2007, pp.&#160;7–10</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=European+Science+Foundation+Position+Paper+Impacts+of+Climate+Change+on+the+European+Marine+and+Coastal+Environment+%E2%80%94+Ecosystems+Approach&amp;rft.pages=7-10&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.esf.org%2Fpublications%2Fposition-papers.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "There is now convincing evidence that since the industrial revolution, human activities, resulting in increasing concentrations of greenhouse gases have become a major agent of climate change. These greenhouse gases affect the global climate by retaining heat in the troposphere, thus raising the average temperature of the planet and altering global atmospheric circulation and precipitation patterns.  While on-going national and international actions to curtail and reduce greenhouse gas emissions are essential, the levels of greenhouse gases currently in the atmosphere, and their impact, are likely to persist for several decades. On-going and increased efforts to mitigate climate change through reduction in greenhouse gases are therefore crucial."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-caets-69"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-caets_69-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20081210053304/http://www.caets.org/nae/naecaets.nsf/(weblinks)/WSAN-78QL9A?OpenDocument">"Archived copy"</a>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2008-04-18</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Archived+copy&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.caets.org%2Fnae%2Fnaecaets.nsf%2F%28weblinks%29%2FWSAN-78QL9A%3FOpenDocument&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><span class="citation-comment" style="display:none; color:#33aa33; margin-left:0.3em">CS1 maint: Archived copy as title (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_Archived_copy_as_title" title="Category:CS1 maint: Archived copy as title">link</a>) </span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-American_Chemical_Society_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change&#39;&#39;-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-American_Chemical_Society_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change&#39;&#39;_70-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://portal.acs.org/portal/acs/corg/content?_nfpb=true&amp;_pageLabel=PP_SUPERARTICLE&amp;node_id=1907&amp;use_sec=false&amp;sec_url_var=region1&amp;__uuid=0cbd57b5-5766-456d-800b-680b88c1c8bf"><i>American Chemical Society </i>Global Climate Change<i><span></span></i></a></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=American+Chemical+Society+Global+Climate+Change&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fportal.acs.org%2Fportal%2Facs%2Fcorg%2Fcontent%3F_nfpb%3Dtrue%26_pageLabel%3DPP_SUPERARTICLE%26node_id%3D1907%26use_sec%3Dfalse%26sec_url_var%3Dregion1%26&#95;_uuid%3D0cbd57b5-5766-456d-800b-680b88c1c8bf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Careful and comprehensive scientific assessments have clearly demonstrated that the Earth's climate system is changing rapidly in response to growing atmospheric burdens of greenhouse gases and absorbing aerosol particles (IPCC, 2007). There is very little room for doubt that observed climate trends are due to human activities. The threats are serious and action is urgently needed to mitigate the risks of climate change.  The reality of global warming, its current serious and potentially disastrous impacts on Earth system properties, and the key role emissions from human activities play in driving these phenomena have been recognized by earlier versions of this ACS policy statement (ACS, 2004), by other major scientific societies, including the American Geophysical Union (AGU, 2003), the American Meteorological Society (AMS, 2007) and the American Association for the Advancement of Science (AAAS, 2007), and by the U. S. National Academies and ten other leading national academies of science (NA, 2005)."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-American_Institute_of_Physics_Statement_supporting_AGU_statement_on_human-induced_climate_change-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-American_Institute_of_Physics_Statement_supporting_AGU_statement_on_human-induced_climate_change_71-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aip.org/fyi/2004/042.html"><i>American Institute of Physics Statement supporting AGU statement on human-induced climate change</i></a>, 2003</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=American+Institute+of+Physics+Statement+supporting+AGU+statement+on+human-induced+climate+change&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aip.org%2Ffyi%2F2004%2F042.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "The Governing Board of the American Institute of Physics has endorsed a position statement on climate change adopted by the American Geophysical Union (AGU) Council in December 2003."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-American_Physical_Society_Climate_Change_Policy_Statement-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-American_Physical_Society_Climate_Change_Policy_Statement_72-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aps.org/policy/statements/07_1.cfm"><i>American Physical Society Climate Change Policy Statement</i></a>, November 2007</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=American+Physical+Society+Climate+Change+Policy+Statement&amp;rft.date=2007-11&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aps.org%2Fpolicy%2Fstatements%2F07_1.cfm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Emissions of greenhouse gases from human activities are changing the atmosphere in ways that affect the Earth's climate. Greenhouse gases include carbon dioxide as well as methane, nitrous oxide and other gases. They are emitted from fossil fuel combustion and a range of industrial and agricultural processes.  The evidence is incontrovertible: Global warming is occurring. If no mitigating actions are taken, significant disruptions in the Earth's physical and ecological systems, social systems, security and human health are likely to occur. We must reduce emissions of greenhouse gases beginning now.  Because the complexity of the climate makes accurate prediction difficult, the APS urges an enhanced effort to understand the effects of human activity on the Earth's climate, and to provide the technological options for meeting the climate challenge in the near and longer terms. The APS also urges governments, universities, national laboratories and its membership to support policies and actions that will reduce the emission of greenhouse gases.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AIP_science_policy_document.-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AIP_science_policy_document._73-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aip.org.au/scipolicy/Science%20Policy.pdf"><i>AIP science policy document.</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, 2005</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=AIP+science+policy+document.&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aip.org.au%2Fscipolicy%2FScience%2520Policy.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Policy: The AIP supports a reduction of the green house gas emissions that are leading to increased global temperatures, and encourages research that works towards this goal.  Reason: Research in Australia and overseas shows that an increase in global temperature will adversely affect the Earth's climate patterns. The melting of the polar ice caps, combined with thermal expansion, will lead to rises in sea levels that may impact adversely on our coastal cities. The impact of these changes on <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> will fundamentally change the <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a> of Earth."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-EPS_Position_Paper_&#39;&#39;Energy_for_the_future:_The_Nuclear_Option&#39;&#39;-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-EPS_Position_Paper_&#39;&#39;Energy_for_the_future:_The_Nuclear_Option&#39;&#39;_74-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://archive.iupap.org/epspositionpaper.pdf"><i>EPS Position Paper </i>Energy for the future: The Nuclear Option<i><span></span></i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, 2007</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=EPS+Position+Paper+Energy+for+the+future%3A+The+Nuclear+Option&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Farchive.iupap.org%2Fepspositionpaper.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "The emission of anthropogenic greenhouse gases, among which carbon dioxide is the main contributor, has amplified the natural greenhouse effect and led to global warming. The main contribution stems from burning fossil fuels. A further increase will have decisive effects on life on earth. An energy cycle with the lowest possible CO<sub>2</sub> emission is called for wherever possible to combat climate change."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Ledley, Tamara S.; Sundquist, Eric T.; Schwartz, Stephen E.; Hall, Dorothy K.; Fellows, Jack D.; Killeen, Timothy L. (September 28, 1999). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20161009000325/http://www.ecd.bnl.gov/pubs/BNL66903.pdf">"Climate Change and Greenhouse Gases"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>EOS</i>. <b>80</b> (39): 453–454, 457–458. <a href="/wiki/Bibcode" title="Bibcode">Bibcode</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1999EOSTr..80Q.453L">1999EOSTr..80Q.453L</a>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1029%2F99EO00325">10.1029/99EO00325</a>.
