<li id="cite_note-www12-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-www12_93-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wmo.ch/pages/mediacentre/statann/documents/SG21_2006_E.pdf">"WMO's Statement at the Twelfth Session of the Conference of the Parties to the U.N. Framework Convention on Climate Change"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=WMO%27s+Statement+at+the+Twelfth+Session+of+the+Conference+of+the+Parties+to+the+U.N.+Framework+Convention+on+Climate+Change.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.wmo.ch%2Fpages%2Fmediacentre%2Fstatann%2Fdocuments%2FSG21_2006_E.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-agu13-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-agu13_94-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.agu.org/fora/eos/pdfs/2006EO360008.pdf">"AGU - American Geophysical Union"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>AGU</i>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=AGU&amp;rft.atitle=AGU+-+American+Geophysical+Union&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.agu.org%2Ffora%2Feos%2Fpdfs%2F2006EO360008.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-inqua-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-inqua_95-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-inqua_95-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.inqua.org/files/iscc.pdf">"INQUA Statement On Climate Change"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=INQUA+Statement+On+Climate+Change.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.inqua.org%2Ffiles%2Fiscc.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-AAWV_&#39;&#39;Position_Statement_on_Climate_Change,_Wildlife_Diseases,_and_Wildlife_Health&#39;&#39;-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AAWV_&#39;&#39;Position_Statement_on_Climate_Change,_Wildlife_Diseases,_and_Wildlife_Health&#39;&#39;_96-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://google.com/search?q=cache:IeEiaoU5hZAJ:www.aawv.net/AAWVPositionClimateChangeFinal.doc+AAWV+Position+Statements+wildlife+diseases+and+wildlife+health&amp;hl=en&amp;ct=clnk&amp;cd=1&amp;gl=us"><i>AAWV </i>Position Statement on Climate Change, Wildlife Diseases, and Wildlife Health<i><span></span></i></a></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=AAWV+Position+Statement+on+Climate+Change%2C+Wildlife+Diseases%2C+and+Wildlife+Health&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fgoogle.com%2Fsearch%3Fq%3Dcache%3AIeEiaoU5hZAJ%3Awww.aawv.net%2FAAWVPositionClimateChangeFinal.doc%2BAAWV%2BPosition%2BStatements%2Bwildlife%2Bdiseases%2Band%2Bwildlife%2Bhealth%26hl%3Den%26ct%3Dclnk%26cd%3D1%26gl%3Dus&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "There is widespread scientific agreement that the world's climate is changing and that the weight of evidence demonstrates that <a href="/wiki/Human_impact_on_the_environment" title="Human impact on the environment">anthropogenic</a> factors have and will continue to contribute significantly to global warming and climate change. It is anticipated that continuing changes to the climate will have serious negative impacts on public, animal and ecosystem health due to <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events, changing <a href="/wiki/Disease_transmission" class="mw-redirect" title="Disease transmission">disease transmission</a> dynamics, emerging and re-emerging <a href="/wiki/Diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Diseases">diseases</a>, and alterations to <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitat</a> and ecological systems that are essential to <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_conservation" title="Wildlife conservation">wildlife conservation</a>. Furthermore, there is increasing recognition of the inter-relationships of human, <a href="/wiki/Domestic_animal" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic animal">domestic animal</a>, wildlife, and ecosystem health as illustrated by the fact the majority of recent emerging diseases have a wildlife origin."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AIBS_Position_Statements-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AIBS_Position_Statements_97-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aibs.org/position-statements"><i>AIBS Position Statements</i></a></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=AIBS+Position+Statements&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aibs.org%2Fposition-statements&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Observations throughout the world make it clear that climate change is occurring, and rigorous scientific research demonstrates that the greenhouse gases emitted by human activities are the primary driver."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Scientific_societies_warn_Senate:_climate_change_is_real-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Scientific_societies_warn_Senate:_climate_change_is_real_98-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://arstechnica.com/tech-policy/news/2009/10/scientific-societies-warn-senate-climate-change-is-real.ars"><i><span></span></i>Scientific societies warn Senate: climate change is real<i><span></span></i></a>, Ars Technica, October 22, 2009</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Scientific+societies+warn+Senate%3A+climate+change+is+real&amp;rft.pub=Ars+Technica&amp;rft.date=2009-10-22&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farstechnica.com%2Ftech-policy%2Fnews%2F2009%2F10%2Fscientific-societies-warn-senate-climate-change-is-real.ars&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Letter_to_US_Senators-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Letter_to_US_Senators_99-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aaas.org/news/releases/2009/media/1021climate_letter.pdf"><i>Letter to US Senators</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, October 2009</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Letter+to+US+Senators&amp;rft.date=2009-10&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aaas.org%2Fnews%2Freleases%2F2009%2Fmedia%2F1021climate_letter.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Global_Environmental_Change_—_Microbial_Contributions,_Microbial_Solutions-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Global_Environmental_Change_—_Microbial_Contributions,_Microbial_Solutions_100-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.asm.org/images/docfilename/0000006005/globalwarming%5B1%5D.pdf"><i>Global Environmental Change — Microbial Contributions, Microbial Solutions</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, <a href="/wiki/American_Society_For_Microbiology" class="mw-redirect" title="American Society For Microbiology">American Society For Microbiology</a>, May 2006</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Global+Environmental+Change+%E2%80%94+Microbial+Contributions%2C+Microbial+Solutions&amp;rft.pub=American+Society+For+Microbiology&amp;rft.date=2006-05&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.asm.org%2Fimages%2Fdocfilename%2F0000006005%2Fglobalwarming%255B1%255D.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> They recommended "reducing net anthropogenic CO<sub>2</sub> emissions to the atmosphere" and "minimizing anthropogenic disturbances of" atmospheric gases.  Carbon dioxide concentrations were relatively stable for the past 10,000 years but then began to increase rapidly about 150 years ago…as a result of fossil fuel consumption and land use change.  Of course, changes in atmospheric composition are but one component of global change, which also includes disturbances in the physical and chemical conditions of the oceans and land surface. Although global change has been a natural process throughout Earth's history, humans are responsible for substantially accelerating present-day changes. These changes may adversely affect human health and the <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">biosphere</a> on which we depend.  Outbreaks of a number of diseases, including <a href="/wiki/Lyme_disease" title="Lyme disease">Lyme disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hantavirus_infections" class="mw-redirect" title="Hantavirus infections">hantavirus infections</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">dengue fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">bubonic plague</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a>, have been linked to climate change."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Australian_Coral_Reef_Society_official_letter-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Australian_Coral_Reef_Society_official_letter_101-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060322170802/http://www.australiancoralreefsociety.org/pdf/chadwick605a.pdf"><i>Australian Coral Reef Society official letter</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, 2006, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.australiancoralreefsociety.org/pdf/chadwick605a.pdf">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 22 March 2006</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Australian+Coral+Reef+Society+official+letter&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.australiancoralreefsociety.org%2Fpdf%2Fchadwick605a.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> Official communique regarding the <a href="/wiki/Great_Barrier_Reef" title="Great Barrier Reef">Great Barrier Reef</a> and the "world-wide decline in <a href="/wiki/Coral_reefs" class="mw-redirect" title="Coral reefs">coral reefs</a> through processes such as <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a>, runoff of nutrients from the land, <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">coral bleaching</a>, global climate change, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>", etc.:  There is almost total <a href="/wiki/Consensus" class="mw-redirect" title="Consensus">consensus</a> among experts that the earth's climate is changing as a result of the build-up of greenhouse gases. The IPCC (involving over 3,000 of the world's experts) has come out with clear conclusions as to the reality of this phenomenon. One does not have to look further than the collective <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy of Sciences">academy of scientists</a> worldwide to see the string (of) statements on this worrying change to the earth's atmosphere.  There is broad scientific consensus that coral reefs are heavily affected by the activities of man and there are significant global influences that can make reefs more vulnerable such as global warming....It is highly likely that coral bleaching has been exacerbated by global warming."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-iob-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-iob_102-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.iob.org/general.asp?section=science_policy/policy_issues&amp;article=climate_change.xml"><i>Institute of Biology policy page ‘Climate Change’</i></a></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Institute+of+Biology+policy+page+%E2%80%98Climate+Change%E2%80%99&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.iob.org%2Fgeneral.asp%3Fsection%3Dscience_policy%2Fpolicy_issues%26article%3Dclimate_change.xml&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/>  "there is scientific agreement that the rapid global warming that has occurred in recent years is mostly anthropogenic, <i>ie</i> due to human activity."  As a consequence of global warming, they warn that a "rise in sea levels due to melting of ice caps is expected to occur. Rises in temperature will have complex and frequently localised effects on weather, but an overall increase in extreme weather conditions and changes in precipitation patterns are probable, resulting in flooding and drought. The spread of <a href="/wiki/Tropical_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical diseases">tropical diseases</a> is also expected."   Subsequently, the Institute of Biology advocates policies to reduce "greenhouse gas emissions, as we feel that the consequences of climate change are likely to be severe."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-SAF_&#39;&#39;Forest_Management_and_Climate_Change_&#39;&#39;-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SAF_&#39;&#39;Forest_Management_and_Climate_Change_&#39;&#39;_103-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.safnet.org/policyandpresspsst/climate_change_expires12-8-2013.pdf"><i>SAF </i>Forest Management and Climate Change <i><span></span></i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, 2008</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=SAF+Forest+Management+and+Climate+Change+&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.safnet.org%2Fpolicyandpresspsst%2Fclimate_change_expires12-8-2013.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Forests are shaped by climate....Changes in temperature and precipitation regimes therefore have the potential to dramatically affect forests nationwide. There is growing evidence that our climate is changing. The changes in temperature have been associated with increasing concentrations of atmospheric carbon dioxide (CO<sub>2</sub>) and other GHGs in the atmosphere."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-SAF_&#39;&#39;Forest_Offset_Projects_in_a_Carbon_Trading_System&#39;&#39;-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SAF_&#39;&#39;Forest_Offset_Projects_in_a_Carbon_Trading_System&#39;&#39;_104-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.safnet.org/policyandpresspsst/offset_projections_expires12-8-2013.pdf"><i>SAF </i>Forest Offset Projects in a Carbon Trading System<i><span></span></i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, 2008</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=SAF+Forest+Offset+Projects+in+a+Carbon+Trading+System&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.safnet.org%2Fpolicyandpresspsst%2Foffset_projections_expires12-8-2013.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Forests play a significant role in offsetting CO<sub>2</sub> emissions, the primary anthropogenic GHG."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Wildlife_Society_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change_and_Wildlife&#39;&#39;-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Wildlife_Society_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change_and_Wildlife&#39;&#39;_105-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20081127232217/http://joomla.wildlife.org/documents/positionstatements/35-Global%20Climate%20Change%20and%20Wildlife.pdf"><i>Wildlife Society </i>Global Climate Change and Wildlife<i><span></span></i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://joomla.wildlife.org/documents/positionstatements/35-Global%20Climate%20Change%20and%20Wildlife.pdf">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 2008-11-27</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Wildlife+Society+Global+Climate+Change+and+Wildlife&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fjoomla.wildlife.org%2Fdocuments%2Fpositionstatements%2F35-Global%2520Climate%2520Change%2520and%2520Wildlife.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Scientists throughout the world have concluded that climate research conducted in the past two decades definitively shows that rapid worldwide climate change occurred in the 20th century, and will likely continue to occur for decades to come. Although climates have varied dramatically since the Earth was formed, few scientists question the role of humans in exacerbating recent climate change through the emission of greenhouse gases. The critical issue is no longer "if" climate change is occurring, but rather how to address its effects on <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">wildlife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_habitat" class="mw-redirect" title="Wildlife habitat">wildlife habitats</a>."  The statement goes on to assert that "evidence is accumulating that wildlife and wildlife habitats have been and will continue to be significantly affected by ongoing large-scale rapid climate change."  The statement concludes with a call for "reduction in anthropogenic (human-caused) sources of carbon dioxide and other greenhouse gas emissions contributing to global climate change and the conservation of CO<sub>2</sub>- consuming <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthesizers</a> (i.e., plants)."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AAP_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change_and_Children&#39;s_Health&#39;&#39;-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AAP_&#39;&#39;Global_Climate_Change_and_Children&#39;s_Health&#39;&#39;_106-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090722104801/http://aappolicy.aappublications.org/cgi/content/full/pediatrics;120/5/1149"><i>AAP </i>Global Climate Change and Children's Health<i><span></span></i></a>, 2007, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://aappolicy.aappublications.org/cgi/content/full/pediatrics;120/5/1149">the original</a> on 2009-07-22<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">2009-02-13</span></span></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=AAP+Global+Climate+Change+and+Children%27s+Health&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Faappolicy.aappublications.org%2Fcgi%2Fcontent%2Ffull%2Fpediatrics%3B120%2F5%2F1149&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "There is broad scientific consensus that Earth's climate is warming rapidly and at an accelerating rate. Human activities, primarily the burning of fossil fuels, are very likely (&gt;90% probability) to be the main cause of this warming. Climate-sensitive changes in ecosystems are already being observed, and fundamental, potentially irreversible, ecological changes may occur in the coming decades. Conservative environmental estimates of the impact of climate changes that are already in process indicate that they will result in numerous health effects to children.  Anticipated direct health consequences of climate change include injury and death from <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather_events" class="mw-redirect" title="Extreme weather events">extreme weather events</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_disasters" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural disasters">natural disasters</a>, increases in climate-sensitive <a href="/wiki/Infectious_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Infectious diseases">infectious diseases</a>, increases in <a href="/wiki/Air_Pollutions_Effect_on_Pulmonary_diseases_and_Children" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Pollutions Effect on Pulmonary diseases and Children">air pollution–related illness</a>, and more heat-related, potentially fatal, illness. Within all of these categories, children have increased vulnerability compared with other groups."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-ACPM_Policy_Statement_&#39;&#39;Abrupt_Climate_Change_and_Public_Health_Implications&#39;&#39;-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ACPM_Policy_Statement_&#39;&#39;Abrupt_Climate_Change_and_Public_Health_Implications&#39;&#39;_107-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071107145339/https://www.acpm.org/2006-002(C).htm"><i>ACPM Policy Statement </i>Abrupt Climate Change and Public Health Implications<i><span></span></i></a>, 2006, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.acpm.org/2006-002(C).htm">the original</a> on 2007-11-07<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">2008-11-21</span></span></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=ACPM+Policy+Statement+Abrupt+Climate+Change+and+Public+Health+Implications&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.acpm.org%2F2006-002%28C%29.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "The American College of Preventive Medicine (ACPM) accept the position that global warming and climate change is occurring, that there is potential for abrupt climate change, and that human practices that increase greenhouse gases exacerbate the problem, and that the <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> consequences may be severe."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-American_Medical_Association_Policy_Statement-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-American_Medical_Association_Policy_Statement_108-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ama-assn.org/ama/pub/category/20275.html"><i>American Medical Association Policy Statement</i></a>, 2008</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=American+Medical+Association+Policy+Statement&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ama-assn.org%2Fama%2Fpub%2Fcategory%2F20275.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Support the findings of the latest Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change report, which states that the Earth is undergoing adverse global climate change and that these changes will negatively affect public health.  Support educating the medical community on the potential adverse public health effects of global climate change, including topics such as population displacement, flooding, infectious and vector-borne diseases, and healthy water supplies."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-apha-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-apha_109-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20091231060829/http://www.apha.org/advocacy/policy/policysearch/default.htm?id=1351"><i>American Public Health Association Policy Statement ‘’Addressing the Urgent Threat of Global Climate Change to Public Health and the Environment’’</i></a>, 2007, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.apha.org/advocacy/policy/policysearch/default.htm?id=1351">the original</a> on 2009-12-31</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=American+Public+Health+Association+Policy+Statement+%E2%80%98%E2%80%99Addressing+the+Urgent+Threat+of+Global+Climate+Change+to+Public+Health+and+the+Environment%E2%80%99%E2%80%99&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.apha.org%2Fadvocacy%2Fpolicy%2Fpolicysearch%2Fdefault.htm%3Fid%3D1351&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "The long-term threat of global climate change to global health is extremely serious and the fourth IPCC report and other scientific literature demonstrate convincingly that anthropogenic <a href="/wiki/GHG_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="GHG emissions">GHG emissions</a> are primarily responsible for this threat….US policy makers should immediately take necessary steps to reduce US emissions of GHGs, including carbon dioxide, to avert dangerous climate change."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AMA_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_Human_Health_—_2004&#39;&#39;-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AMA_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_Human_Health_—_2004&#39;&#39;_110-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://fed.ama.com.au/cms/web.nsf/doc/WOOD-5ZD6BT"><i>AMA </i>Climate Change and Human Health — 2004<i><span></span></i></a>, 2004</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=AMA+Climate+Change+and+Human+Health+%E2%80%94+2004&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Ffed.ama.com.au%2Fcms%2Fweb.nsf%2Fdoc%2FWOOD-5ZD6BT&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since January 2018">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup> They recommend policies "to mitigate the possible consequential health effects of climate change through improved energy efficiency, clean energy production and other emission reduction steps."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AMA_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_Human_Health&#39;&#39;_—_2004._Revised_2008.-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AMA_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_Human_Health&#39;&#39;_—_2004._Revised_2008._111-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090216083701/http://ama.com.au/node/4442"><i>AMA </i>Climate Change and Human Health<i> — 2004. Revised 2008.</i></a>, 2008, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ama.com.au/node/4442">the original</a> on 2009-02-16</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=AMA+Climate+Change+and+Human+Health+%E2%80%94+2004.+Revised+2008.&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ama.com.au%2Fnode%2F4442&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "The world's climate – our life-support system – is being altered in ways that are likely to pose significant direct and indirect challenges to health. While ‘climate change’ can be due to natural forces or human activity, there is now substantial evidence to indicate that human activity – and specifically increased greenhouse gas (GHGs) emissions – is a key factor in the pace and extent of global temperature increases.  Health impacts of climate change include the direct impacts of extreme events such as storms, floods, <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heatwaves</a> and fires and the indirect effects of longer-term changes, such as drought, changes to the <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a>, resource conflicts and population shifts.  Increases in average temperatures mean that alterations in the geographic range and seasonality of certain infections and diseases (including vector-borne diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dengue_fever" title="Dengue fever">dengue fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ross_River_virus" title="Ross River virus">Ross River virus</a> and food-borne infections such as <a href="/wiki/Salmonellosis" title="Salmonellosis">Salmonellosis</a>) may be among the first detectable impacts of climate change on human health.  Human health is ultimately dependent on the health of the planet and its ecosystem. The AMA believes that measures which mitigate climate change will also benefit public health. Reducing GHGs should therefore be seen as a public health priority."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-wfpha-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-wfpha_112-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20081217173936/http://www.wfpha.org/Archives/01.22%20Global%20Climate%20Change.pdf"><i>World Federation of Public Health Associations resolution "Global Climate Change"</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, 2001, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wfpha.org/Archives/01.22%20Global%20Climate%20Change.pdf">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 2008-12-17</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=World+Federation+of+Public+Health+Associations+resolution+%22Global+Climate+Change%22&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.wfpha.org%2FArchives%2F01.22%2520Global%2520Climate%2520Change.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Noting the conclusions of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>' Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) and other climatologists that anthropogenic greenhouse gases, which contribute to global climate change, have substantially increased in atmospheric concentration beyond natural processes and have increased by 28 percent since the industrial revolution….Realizing that subsequent health effects from such perturbations in the climate system would likely include an increase in: heat-related mortality and morbidity; vector-borne infectious diseases,… <a href="/wiki/Water-borne_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Water-borne diseases">water-borne diseases</a>…(and) malnutrition from threatened agriculture….the World Federation of Public Health Associations…recommends precautionary primary preventive measures to avert climate change, including reduction of greenhouse gas emissions and preservation of greenhouse gas sinks through appropriate energy and land use policies, in view of the scale of potential health impacts...."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-WHO_&#39;&#39;Protecting_health_from_climate_change&#39;&#39;-113"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-WHO_&#39;&#39;Protecting_health_from_climate_change&#39;&#39;_113-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/world-health-day/toolkit/report_web.pdf"><i>WHO </i>Protecting health from climate change<i><span></span></i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, 2008, p.&#160;2<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">2009-04-18</span></span></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=WHO+Protecting+health+from+climate+change&amp;rft.pages=2&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.who.int%2Fworld-health-day%2Ftoolkit%2Freport_web.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Statement_supporting_AGU_statement_on_human-induced_climate_change-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Statement_supporting_AGU_statement_on_human-induced_climate_change_114-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070507060001/http://www.aas.org/governance/council/resolutions.php#climate"><i>Statement supporting AGU statement on human-induced climate change</i></a>, American Astronomical Society, 2004, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aas.org/governance/council/resolutions.php#climate">the original</a> on 2007-05-07</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Statement+supporting+AGU+statement+on+human-induced+climate+change&amp;rft.pub=American+Astronomical+Society&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aas.org%2Fgovernance%2Fcouncil%2Fresolutions.php%23climate&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "In endorsing the "Human Impacts on Climate" statement [issued by the American Geophysical Union], the AAS recognizes the collective expertise of the AGU in scientific subfields central to assessing and understanding global change, and acknowledges the strength of agreement among our AGU colleagues that the global climate is changing and human activities are contributing to that change."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-ASA_Statement_on_Climate_Change-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ASA_Statement_on_Climate_Change_115-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.amstat.org/news/climatechange.cfm"><i>ASA Statement on Climate Change</i></a>, November 30, 2007</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=ASA+Statement+on+Climate+Change&amp;rft.date=2007-11-30&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.amstat.org%2Fnews%2Fclimatechange.cfm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "The ASA endorses the IPCC conclusions.... Over the course of four assessment reports, a small number of statisticians have served as authors or reviewers. Although this involvement is encouraging, it does not represent the full range of statistical expertise available. ASA recommends that more statisticians should become part of the IPCC process. Such participation would be mutually beneficial to the assessment of climate change and its impacts and also to the statistical community."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-116">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Lapp, David. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.engineerscanada.ca/climate-change">"What Is Climate Change"</a>. <i>Canadian Council of Professional Engineers</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">18 August</span> 2015</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Canadian+Council+of+Professional+Engineers&amp;rft.atitle=What+Is+Climate+Change&amp;rft.aulast=Lapp&amp;rft.aufirst=David&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.engineerscanada.ca%2Fclimate-change&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Policy_Statement,_Climate_Change_and_Energy-117"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Policy_Statement,_Climate_Change_and_Energy_117-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.engineersaustralia.org.au/representation/policy-positions/climate-change.cfm"><i>Policy Statement, Climate Change and Energy</i></a>, February 2007</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Policy+Statement%2C+Climate+Change+and+Energy&amp;rft.date=2007-02&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.engineersaustralia.org.au%2Frepresentation%2Fpolicy-positions%2Fclimate-change.cfm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Engineers Australia believes that Australia must act swiftly and proactively in line with global expectations to address climate change as an economic, social and environmental risk... We believe that addressing the costs of atmospheric emissions will lead to increasing our competitive advantage by minimising risks and creating new economic opportunities. Engineers Australia believes the Australian Government should ratify the Kyoto Protocol."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-IAGLR_Fact_Sheet_&#39;&#39;The_Great_Lakes_at_a_Crossroads:_Preparing_for_a_Changing_Climate&#39;&#39;-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-IAGLR_Fact_Sheet_&#39;&#39;The_Great_Lakes_at_a_Crossroads:_Preparing_for_a_Changing_Climate&#39;&#39;_118-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.iaglr.org/scipolicy/factsheets/iaglr_crossroads_climatechange.pdf"><i>IAGLR Fact Sheet </i>The Great Lakes at a Crossroads: Preparing for a Changing Climate<i><span></span></i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, February 2009</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=IAGLR+Fact+Sheet+The+Great+Lakes+at+a+Crossroads%3A+Preparing+for+a+Changing+Climate&amp;rft.date=2009-02&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.iaglr.org%2Fscipolicy%2Ffactsheets%2Fiaglr_crossroads_climatechange.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "While the Earth's climate has changed many times during the planet's history because of natural factors, including volcanic eruptions and changes in the Earth's orbit, never before have we observed the present rapid rise in temperature and carbon dioxide (CO<sub>2</sub>).  Human activities resulting from the industrial revolution have changed the chemical composition of the atmosphere....Deforestation is now the second largest contributor to global warming, after the burning of fossil fuels. These human activities have significantly increased the concentration of "greenhouse gases" in the atmosphere.  As the Earth's climate warms, we are seeing many changes: stronger, more destructive hurricanes; heavier rainfall; more disastrous flooding; more areas of the world experiencing severe drought; and more heat waves."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-IPENZ_Informatory_Note,_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_the_greenhouse_effect&#39;&#39;-119"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-IPENZ_Informatory_Note,_&#39;&#39;Climate_Change_and_the_greenhouse_effect&#39;&#39;_119-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ipenz.org.nz/ipenz/forms/pdfs/Info_Note_6.pdf"><i>IPENZ Informatory Note, </i>Climate Change and the greenhouse effect<i><span></span></i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, October 2001</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=IPENZ+Informatory+Note%2C+Climate+Change+and+the+greenhouse+effect&amp;rft.date=2001-10&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ipenz.org.nz%2Fipenz%2Fforms%2Fpdfs%2FInfo_Note_6.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> "Human activities have increased the concentration of these atmospheric greenhouse gases, and although the changes are relatively small, the equilibrium maintained by the atmosphere is delicate, and so the effect of these changes is significant. The world's most important greenhouse gas is carbon dioxide, a by-product of the burning of fossil fuels. Since the time of the Industrial Revolution about 200 years ago, the concentration of carbon dioxide in the atmosphere has increased from about 280 parts per million to 370 parts per million, an increase of around 30%.  On the basis of available data, climate scientists are now projecting an average global temperature rise over this century of 2.0 to 4.5°C. This compared with 0.6°C over the previous century – about a 500% increase... This could lead to changing, and for all emissions scenarios more unpredictable, weather patterns around the world, less frost days, more extreme events (droughts and storm or flood disasters), and warmer sea temperatures and melting glaciers causing sea levels to rise.  ... Professional engineers commonly deal with risk, and frequently have to make judgments based on incomplete data. The available evidence suggests very strongly that human activities have already begun to make significant changes to the earth's climate, and that the long-term risk of delaying action is greater than the cost of avoiding/minimising the risk."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-aapg-120"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-aapg_120-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dpa.aapg.org/gac/statements/climatechange.pdf">AAPG Position Statement: Climate Change</a> from dpa.aapg.org</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-aapg14-121"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-aapg14_121-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aapg.org/explorer/president/2007/03mar.cfm">"Climate :03:2007 EXPLORER"</a>. Aapg.org<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2012-07-30</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Climate+%3A03%3A2007+EXPLORER&amp;rft.pub=Aapg.org&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aapg.org%2Fexplorer%2Fpresident%2F2007%2F03mar.cfm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScientific+opinion+on+climate+change" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-2010_tpgmarapr-122"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2010_tpgmarapr_122-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://64.207.34.58/StaticContent/3/TPGs/2010_TPGMarApr.pdf"><i>Sunsetting the Global Climate Change Committee</i></a>, <i>The Professional Geologist</i>, March/April 2010, p. 28</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-123">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://aipg.org/posstatements">"AIPG Position Statements"</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.
